After I have completed for you, O Sons, this book which is the last in medicine with its complement, and I have reached the end of it through its explanations and declarations, it seemed to me that I should complete it for you with this Treatise which is a part of operation, that is, surgery with the hand.
Since operation with the hand is abandoned in our region and time altogether, so that perhaps its knowledge has perished and its trace has been cut off; and nothing remains of it except for small descriptions in the books of the ancients, which have been changed by hands; and errors and hesitations occurred to them, until their intentions were closed and their strength was weakened. It seemed to me that I should revive it with the arrangement of this Treatise on it according to the way of positioning, explanation, and abbreviation; and that I would come with figures of the cautery iron and other instruments for work: as is done by adding explanations and hastening what is necessary.
But the reason why a good artisan of it is not found with his hand in this our time is that the art of medicine is long, and it is necessary for its author to be trained beforehand in the science of anatomy, as Galen narrated, until he knows the supports of the members, and their forms, and their conjunction and separation, and has knowledge of the bones, and nerves, and sinews, and their number, and their exit, and of the pulsatile and quiet veins, and of the exits of these.
And because of this, Hippocrates said that a name with a name is much, and with work it is little, especially in the art of the hand.
But we have already spoken about that at the beginning of this book.
"Since he who is not knowledgeable about what we said regarding anatomy is not purged of error, whereby men are killed: just as I have seen many of those who claim to be formed in this science and boast about it without knowledge or experience.
"Which is to say, I have seen a foolish physician cut out a scrofulous abscess on a woman's neck, and he sliced into some of the arteries in her neck; therefore, the womanâ€™s blood flowed until she died in his hands.
"And I have seen another physician who presumed to remove a stone from a man who had grown old, and the stone was large. "He came to him and removed it along with a piece of the bladder. "Wherefore the man died on the third day.
"And I was called to remove it, and seeing the great size of the stone and the condition of the patient, I knew that he would die.
"And I have seen another physician who received payment from a certain Duke of our land for his medical service: and it happened to a black eunuch who was with him that he suffered a fracture in his leg near the ankle; and the physician, in his ignorance, hastily bound the fracture over the wound with bandages and strong clamps, allowing no air to reach the wound.
"Then he released him according to his wishes. "After that, he released him after a few days and ordered him not to loosen the bandage; and so it remained until his leg became gangrenous, along with his foot, leading to its destruction.
"So I was called to him and hastened to loosen the bandage; and he found relief and was freed from his pains.
"But the corruption in the limb had already taken hold, and I could not stop it.
Therefore, the corruption ceased to walk in the limb until it died.
And I saw another physician who pierced a cancerous abscess, and it became ulcerated after several days until the evil of it was greatly increased with its lord.
That is, because when the cancer is pure of black bile, then it is not necessary to approach it with iron at all unless it is in a member that can bear it, so that all of it may be cut off.
And because of this, O sons, it is necessary for you to know that the surgical operation is divided into two divisions: namely, the operation associated with health and the operation which involves danger in many dispositions.
And I have already pointed out in every place of this book where an operation occurs which involves fear and dread.
Therefore it is necessary for you to beware of that and to avoid it, so that the foolish may not find a way to speak about it and dishonor it.
Receive then the measure with diligence and caution, and your sick with ease and steadfastness, and use the better way which leads by the grace of God to health and praiseworthy success: and leave behind terrible diseases of difficult cure; and lift up your spirits from that which makes you fearful, so that hesitation may not come upon you in your faith and interest.
For it remains more for your glory, and is higher in this world, and finally to the degree of your abilities.
For Galen has already said in some of his advice. Do not treat the bad disease, lest you be called a bad physician.
Now, however, I have divided this Treatise into three Chapters.
Chapter One.
On Cautery with Fire, and Cautery with Sharp Medicine, this Chapter is arranged and ordered from the head to the feet, including the shapes of the instruments and tools for cautery, and everything necessary for the operation.
Chapter Two.
About incision and perforation, bloodletting and ventoses, and wounds: about the extraction of arrows and similar things: and all this is arranged according to the forms of the instruments.
Chapter Three.
About restoration and dislocation, and the cure of wrenching, and similar things: arranged from head to foot, according to the forms of the instruments.
But before I remind you of the procedure with it, it is necessary for me to say about its benefits and harms, and in which temperament it should be administered.
Therefore, I say that the discussion about the quality of the help and harm of cautery is a lengthy and subtle science, and an obscure secret.
Many wise men have also spoken about it and disagreed about it, and for me, a little from their discussions is enough, fearing prolixity. âœ¨
Therefore, I say that cautery benefits every temperament, whether material or immaterial, except for two temperaments: the hot temperament without matter and the dry temperament without matter.
About the hot and dry temperament with matter, they disagreed. For some said that cautery is helpful in it. âœ¨ âœ¨ âœ¨ And others said the opposite of this, namely that cautery is not suitable in an illness caused by heat and dryness; for the nature of fire is heat, and it is inconvenient to cure a hot and dry illness with heat and dryness.
And he who speaks against this said that cautery is beneficial in every warm and dry illness that occurs in the human body; for when you compare the human body and its moistures to the complexion of fire, you find the human body to be cold.
And I say through his speech: for experiment has already revealed this to me many times.
However, it is not fitting that anyone should approach this unless he has already been tested and trained in the final exercise of the chapter on cautery, and has recognized the diversity of human complexions, and the nature of illnesses in themselves, and their causes, and their accidents, and their duration.
As for the other complexions, there is no need to fear; especially in cold and moist illnesses. For all physicians have agreed on these matters and have not disagreed with the use of cautery in them.
And know, my sons, that the secret of cure by means of a cautery with fire and its efficacy over a cautery with combustible medicine is that fire is simple, whose action does not extend except to the member that is cauterized; and it does no harm to another member joined with it, except for a slight injury. xspace
But the action of combustible medicine reaches even what is remote from the members; and perhaps it causes illness of difficult cure in a member, and perhaps it kills.  xspace  xspace
But fire, because of its subtlety and the goodness of its substance, does not do this except in excess.
Now indeed this has been made known to us through experience because of the length of our service and study in the art, and our dedication to the truth; and for that reason I am excused from prolonging the discussion.
And if it were not allowed to this book of mine, I would bring you the secret hidden in fire and the quality of its operation in bodies for the purpose of expelling illnesses, demonstrated by a persuasive philosophical speech that would be accepted by your minds.
And know, children, that they disagree about the time when it is best to perform cautery, and they say that spring is the better time.
And I say that cautery is appropriate at all times because the harm that occurs due to the time is overshadowed by the benefit that is drawn from the cautery. And especially if the cautery is due to severe, urgent pains that do not tolerate delay; because it is feared from them that a worse outcome will occur than the slight harm caused by timing.
And do not let it enter your minds, O children, that only the ignorant and foolish physicians believe that the illness treated by cautery does not always recur; and they conclude this, but it is not as they think. Because cautery is nothing other than a remedy which alters the complexion and dries up the humors which are the cause of the pains.
However, cautery is superior to medicine because of its quick effectiveness, the power of its action, and the intensity of its control. And it is possible that the illness may return at some point in time according to the constitution of the patient, the nature of his illness, its strength, what is prepared in his body from the accumulation of superfluous matter, and what reaches him through food and similar causes, unless the illness for which cautery is applied is fatal.
A subtle illness of a member with few superfluities and humors, such as tooth cautery for pain and similar conditions, it is possible that the pain may not return. "But that occurs rarely.
But the common saying again is true, that cautery is the last resort of medicine; and their intention is not as they themselves intend in it, for they believe that no treatment can be applied together with medicine after the effect of cautery.
But the truth is contrary to that saying, and the meaning, that cautery is the last resort of medicine, does not exist except in this sense: when we administer treatment methods for some diseases and they do not help, then at the end we apply cautery, and it helps; thus it follows that cautery is the last resort of medicine, not according to the intention that the common people and many stupid physicians understand.
The ancients said that cautery with gold is better than cautery with iron; and they did not say this except because of the balance of gold and the nobility of its substance; and they said that cautery does not cause suppuration in the place where it is applied. However, that is not absolutely true; for I have already tested it and found that cautery itself does not do this in some bodies without other factors involved.
And cautery with gold is good, and better than with iron, as they said. Nevertheless, when you cauterize with fire from gold, the fire does not show you when it is ignited to the degree that you wish, because of the redness of the gold; and when it quickly turns cold, if you add more fire upon it, it melts in the fire and turns into plates.
Therefore, the craftsman falls short in that respect; and because of this, cautery with iron is faster and more convenient for us, in terms of correct practice.
And I have indeed already arranged this chapter on cautery according to chapters, and I have arranged them from head to foot, so that those who seek it may find what they want from it.
"Chapter II.
"This cauterization is beneficial for controlling moisture and cold on the brain: these two conditions are causes of headaches, excessive flow of humors from the head to the eyes and ears, excess sleep, toothache, throat pain, and universally all illnesses arising from coldness, such as paralysis, headaches, epilepsy, apoplexy, and similar diseases.
"The method of cauterization is that you instruct the patient to first empty the head for three or four nights with cleansing medicine, according to the strength of the patient, age, and habit.
"Then instruct him to shave his head with a razor. "Then have him sit upright between your hands, placing his own hands on his chest.
"Then place the base of your palm on the base of his nose between his eyes. "Wherever your middle finger reaches, mark that spot with ink.
"Then heat the cautery in oil. This is its shape.
"Then place it on the marked spot with ink. Gradually lower your hand to press it firmly and rotate it. "Then quickly lift your hand and examine the spot.
"If you see that the area as large as a lentil or a grain of barley has been exposed from the bone, then lift your hand. "And if not, repeat the process with the same iron or another if it cools, until you see the bone as I have told you.
"Then take some salt, dissolve it in water, and soak a cloth in the solution. Place the cloth on the spot and leave it for three days.
Then place a piece of cloth soaked in butter over it and leave it there until the fire burn is destroyed. Then care for it with tetrapharmacon ointment until it heals.
Now they say that the more a wound remains open, the more pus it sends out; therefore it is better and more beneficial.
And some of them said that the skin should be cauterized to the bone, and that the cautery should be held until a thick part of the bone is burned.
Then that part which has been burnt from the bone is scraped away, then it is cleaned out.
And others say that it is necessary to go with the cautery to the very end, until it makes an imprint in the bone like a tem, so that the bone falls away; this happens just as if one were using a kirate or the instrument which women put into alphabet infusions. And they believe that from this place the vapors of the head are expelled and the wound is left open for a long time.
Then it should be cleaned out until it heals over.
But these two types of cautery do not seem to me to be suitable except in some people according to the way of fear.
And to let it go is, in my opinion, better for the patient's health.
For the head is weakened by the dissolution of its natural continuity, as we have shown with other members; and especially when the head of the patient is naturally weak. The first type of cautery is safer and better in my opinion, and that is what I use. So, work with it for the sake of health.
Chapter III
When chronic and persistent pain occurs throughout the entire head, and the patient uses syrups, powders, purges, oils, and fumigations. And especially if it has already been cauterized with that one-pronged iron I mentioned, and nothing else helps: then consider. For if the head of the sick person is of strong and robust nature, not weak, and he finds extreme cold: then cauterize him with a different iron under that one. Then cauterize him over every horn of his head with the iron, so that it does not pierce the skin, and expose the amount of bone I mentioned. And cauterize him with a single iron on the back of his head at a place called 'uas', which is the location where the windpipe is placed. Raise your hand in this manner, and you will not expose bone. For the sick person finds on account of this an intense pain, and different from the pain of all other head cauteries.
And I call this the Cautery in its place. And it is necessary that it be a finer iron than the one used to cauterize the horns of the head and the back of the head.
Chapter IV.
When pain and headache occur in any part of the head, or when the pain extends to the eye and is evacuated with purifying medications, and the rest of the treatment is administered as I mentioned in the divisions of illnesses, but it does not help entirely, then there are two ways to cauterize: either with a sharp burning medicine or with iron. ï¸Ž
Now, to cauterize with a sharp burning medicine, take one clove of garlic and peel it, then cut off its ends from both sides. Then divide the place of pain with a broad lancet, until there is a space under the skin where the tooth can be placed. ï¸Ž
Insert it under the skin until it is hidden; then bind it with a suitable bandage above. Leave it for fifteen hours, then remove it and extract the garlic. Leave the wound open for two or three days; afterwards place a pledget soaked in butter over the wound until pus forms; then treat it with an ointment until it heals.
And if you wish, make this preparation with some of the warming medicines that I have written about in chapter twelve on heating medicines.
To cauterize it with iron is done as follows: The fire brand, which looks like this.
And it is called a "Claw"; because the head of it resembles the shape of a nail with some curvature, and in its middle there is a small projection.
Then place it on the wound and hold your hand firmly; and slowly rotate the iron with speed; and let the amount that is burned be half the thickness of the skin. And raise your hand so that the vein underneath is not burned and bleeding occurs.
Then soak a pledget in salt water and place it on the wound and leave it for three days; then place a pledget with butter; afterwards treat it with an ointment until it heals. ï¸Ž
And if you wish, cauterize this half-head wound with the pointed end of a second cautery. And be careful not to cut an artery in this half-skull, unless it is necessary. ï¸Ž
Â¶ On the method of cauterizing in old half-skulls.
When you are treating half-skull with what we have said in the preceding treatment and in the divisions of diseases, and it does not heal; and you see from the disease that what we have said about cautery with medicine or with a heated iron is not enough, then you should heat a pointed cautery until it whitens after marking the place of pain with a line whose length is half a finger or similar to that; and raise your hand once, and bind it until you cut the artery and reach the bone.
But you must be careful not to burn the side or the nerve that moves the jaw during chewing, lest a spasm occur.
And be on guard against the flow of blood from the cut artery. For its incision is dangerous, especially for one who is ignorant of what he does, unstudious, and inexperienced; and he leaves off the operation with that in particular.
And I shall pardon myself by remembering to give rules for stopping the flow of blood from an artery according to its manner and in the proper place in this book.
But if you see from the illness that this cautery is not enough, and you see the patient's body tolerating a cautery on the middle of the head, as we have said, care for the wound until it heals.
And if you wish, administer the cautery that we have mentioned in the chapter on extracting an artery with a two-bladed knife.  /> For this cautery is better and more beneficial than that one.
Â¶ On the method of cauterizing for earache.
When earache occurs from cold and is treated with solutions and other methods of treatment as we have said in the division, but the pain is not removed, then use fire for cautery; and this is what is called a "Puncture," the form of which is as follows:  />  >
Then, after it is heated by fire, make punctures with it around the entire ear, as shown here: or around both ears if the pain is in both at the same time. And keep the cautery a short distance from the root of the ear after marking the places with the iron: and let there be ten punctures on each ear, as shown here.
Then care for the places until they heal.
In the way of cauterizing in Torture.
Chapter VII.
The torture that is treated with cauterization is not anything other than the types which occur from phlegm, as we have said in the divisions of diseases.
And avoid cauterizing the type that occurs from dryness and nerve spasm.
When you treat this type of torture with medicines, purgatives, gargles, and your treatment does not help, then it is necessary to cauterize the patient with three cauteries: one at the root of the ear, another a little below its tympanum, and the third at the junction of the two lips.
And place your cautery on the opposite side of the diseased part. Because softening does not occur except in the part that appears healthy.
And the manner of cauterization is that you cauterize it with a cautery directly at the tip of the upper ear, a little under the horn of the head: and another one on the tympanum, whose length should be according to the length of the thumb. And place your hand with the cautery until the amount equivalent to half the thickness of the skin is burned.  /> Si quis non est prudens in hac arte, vide ne uelimus, ne uideantur perforationes in ea parte.
And this is the form of the cautery, and it is a species made from an old knife, whose form has been mentioned above; however, it is not a little subtler than what you see: and it is necessary that there be a little excess in the thickness of the knife.
Then treat the places with what was mentioned previously until they heal.
Â¶ On the method of cauterizing for old apoplexy.
When apoplexy becomes chronic and you treat it with what we have mentioned, and your treatment does not help, and the patient has no fever, then cauterize him with four cauteries on every horn of his head, and a cautery in the middle of the head as we said, and a cautery at the back of the head, as previously stated; and let the manner of the cautery be as previously mentioned.  /> Et si fuerit in infirmo fomes, nequeas curare eum: sed poteris curare eum cum cauteriis, et praedicta medicamenta, secundum quod diximus, et si non sanabitur nisi uerecundia tua in deum.
And it is also cauterized with a cautery over the mouth of the stomach; and it is more ultimate.
Then it should be scraped, along with what has preceded.
Chapter IX.
It is necessary that in the first place large henbane seeds and purifying pills for the brain be given to the patient to drink.
Then shave the entire head of the patient and place on his occiput a plaster made from mustard, as described in the treatise on plasters; and apply it several times.
For this is the method of cautery; and do it in the same way as I have said there.
If therefore he is cured by that, it is good. If not, then make three cauteries on the back of his head, which should descend from the upper part of the head to the lower part of the eye; and put the width of a finger between each cautery.
Then treat the cauteries as described above.
If you wish to add more and the patient is able to bear it, then make a cautery in the middle. If you wish to add more, then cauterize him over both temples.
Then treat the patient until he is cured; and let the cautery be oiled according to the shape described above.
On the Method of Cauterization for Paralysis and Softening.
Chapter X.
It is necessary that you proceed with the purification of the head using henbane and as we have said.  /> Â¶ Et sit haec modus Cauterii.
Then shave the patient's head. After that, cauterize him with a cautery in the middle of his head, and with a cautery over each temple, and with a cautery on the back of his head, and with three cauteries on the vertebrae of his neck.  /> Et si fuerit necesse: tunc fac ei cauteria quatuor ad uires eius, et sit illud in capite, et inter oculos, et in medio colli, et in medio thoracis.
If however you need to soothe the body with many of those during illness, and if the patient is weak and the disease is strong: then cauterize him with four cauteries on the vertebrae of the back, and with the last cautery until most of the skin is burned off, and lift your hand. Then care for him until he heals; and thus ends the section on cauterization.
On the manner of cauterizing in epilepsy.
An epileptic is not to be cauterized unless his epilepsy is due to phlegm.
Therefore, it is necessary that you cleanse his brain first with cupping glasses and with the rest of the treatment which we have said in the division, when the patient is large or can tolerate the taking of medicines.
But if he is a child who cannot tolerate medicines, then let him be given gargles and cleansing foods to chew for many days before that, with the improvement of his diet.
Then shave his head; afterward cauterize him with one cautery in the middle of his head, according to what was said before about the manner; and with another cautery on the back of his head, and over each horn of his head with a cautery. But if the patient is strong and can tolerate it, then cauterize him with the cauteries which I mentioned for those with paralysis, and to soothe the body on the vertebrae of the neck and back: and let the final cautery be according to the manner which was said before. ã€‹
But if the patient is a child, then place a fine cautery accordingly.
On the manner of cauterizing in melancholy. ã€‹ ã€‹
When the cause of melancholy is corrupted moisture and thick phlegm, then cauterize him with the cauteries which we mentioned for those with paralysis.
And if the cause of melancholy is an excess of black bile towards melancholy, and the body of the sick person is moist, then give him to drink that which cleanses his brain, according to what preceded in the division: then shave the head of the sick person, and afterwards make a neatly made tortilla from linen, like a circle.
Then place it in the middle of the head; and let the sick person, sitting square, be held on every side.
Then present a poultice. And it is more suitable from old ewe's butter. And heat it over a fire with a moderate amount of warmth, so that when the finger is inserted into it, it may bear it. Then evacuate it onto the middle of his head in a circle, and leave it until it cools.  />  Et quando frigida facta est, tollens illud de capite infirmi, fac quod uelis.
Do this for the sick person once a week with the rest of his good regime until he is cured.
Or if you wish, cauterize it by making many small punctures, except that you hold the hand with the cautery; rather let it be fragrant.
For this kind of cautery moistens the brain with its quality.
Then place upon it a cloth soaked in butter or chicken fat.
Â¶ On the method of cauterizing with water dripping into the eye.
Chapter 13.
When the beginning of water in the eye is declared to you by the signs that I have mentioned in the division, then begin and give the sick person to drink that which cleanses his head.
And keep him away from all moist things, and make him sit in a bathhouse in fasting for several days.
Then instruct him to shave his head, and cauterize it in the middle of his head.  />  Et sit hoc in diebus plurimis: et postea fac eum radere caput suum. Then burn the patient above both temples with two irons, if the water flow is beginning simultaneously in both eyes; or from one side only, if the flow is starting in one eye. And cut off with an iron all veins and arteries that are under the skin: and let the cauteries be long in the breadth of the temples; and take care to prevent the flow of blood.
If you see anything from it, then cut it off immediately with whatever medicine is possible; and I will come with the wisdom which is in the extraction of arteries, and their cutting, and care to prevent the flow of blood.
And sometimes it should be burned on the neck under two bones with two irons fully extended.
Â¶ On the method of burning away old tears.
When the tears of the eyes are old and persistent, and they are over the veins and arteries which are evident on the outer surface of the head, it is verified that this comes from cold, phlegmatic excesses; then burn with the same iron as I described in the case of water starting to flow, with one iron in the middle of the head, and two irons over both temples, and two irons on the neck under two bones. And if you need to add more, then burn the patient carefully on every side of the eye, at the outer edge of the eyebrow with a small iron.
Â¶ On the method of burning away nasal odor.
When you are treating this condition with the method we mentioned in division, and it does not benefit from treatment; then hurry up and give infirmocochias to drink for three nights: then shave his head, and burn him with a medium-sized iron and an olive oil cautery. Then burn the patient with two small irons over both eyebrows under the hair.
And be careful not to cut the artery.
And this is the shape of the cupping glass.
In the manner of cauterizing for the softening of the eyelid.
When the eyelid of the eye is softened by illness or moisture, then cauterize the eyelid with one cautery, and this lunar cautery.
And if you wish, cauterize [the area] above the two eyebrows a little with two cauteries on every side, and let them be distant from the two temples; and let the length of every cautery be according to the length of the eyebrow, and do not touch with your hand the cautery, but according to the amount that the third eyelid is burnt.
In the manner of cauterizing the eyelid when the hairs turn in and prick the eye. )))
There are two ways to cauterize it: either with a hot iron, or with a burning medicine.
But in the case of the hot iron, tell the patient beforehand to let his hairs grow, if he is one of those who plucks them out, until they lengthen and become even. ))) ))) ))) ))) But if they prick him at their origin, then bind his eyes with a bandage, so that they do not move, until they are born. )))
When they are born and become even, then put the patient's head in your lap; then mark on his eyelid with caustic, a mark that should be like the shape of a myrtle leaf; and let the beginning of the mark be near the hairs.
Then place a cloth soaked in egg white, or in slippery elm mucilage, over the eye.
Then, for the cautery iron, which looks like this.
Then cauterize over the figure which you have marked little by little in several places, until the surface of the skin, which is like a myrtle leaf, is entirely burned and appears properly.
And the sign of health in your work is that if you see the eyelid already contracting and the hairs rising at the point of the eye.
Then raise your hand (i.e., stop treating): and leave him for three days.
Then put on him cotton with butter, until the scab is removed. Then treat him with ointment, until he heals.
If any of the hairs returns after an hour and the eyelid softens, then repeat the cautery on that spot as you did at first.
If however the hairs are on the lower (eyelid), then cauterize it until it rises to its natural place and is even so that the hairs do not prick the eye.
It is that you advise the patient to let the hairs grow until they lengthen and even out. ï¸Ž Make from a piece of cloth the shape of a myrtle leaf.
Then take from known soap and from unslaked lime one ounce each or so: then grind them together well until you make that quickly, so it does not cool down. Then spread it over the shape of the myrtle leaf that you have made on the cloth, and place it on the eyelid of one or two eyes. ï¸Ž And put under the eye cotton soaked in egg white; and let the patient's head be in your lap.
And put your index finger on the medicine, and press it slightly. And you shall move it whenever the sick person feels the biting of the medicine, for its biting is like fire.
Therefore, while this biting that he has found persists, then leave off the medicine and move it with your finger. When therefore the biting ceases, then remove the medicine and wash the eye with water.
And consider then, if you see the eyelid lifted up, as it is lifted up with burning or cutting, it is well: and if not, then repeat on that same spot of medicine where it does not make an impression and does not blacken, until your operation is made equal and the eye contracts.
Then place on it Kohl with butter, until the skin of the burn is removed. Then care for it with diaphoretic ointment or another, until it heals.
And it is necessary for you during the operation that you guard with the greatest care, lest anything from the medicine fall into the eye.
But if the eyelid becomes soft after days and something struggles from the hairs into the eye, then repeat the medicine on that spot which is becoming soft from the eyelid, just as you did at first. Then care for it until it heals.
And this is the shape of a myrtle leaf.
And know that human eyes are varied in size and smallness. Therefore let your consideration be according to that, and may the way of righteousness not be hidden from him who has an interest in this art. ã€‹
Â¶ On the Method of Cauterizing the Lacrimal Duct.
When you are treating a fistula with what we have said regarding the divisions of diseases and your treatment is not effective, then it is necessary that you cauterize it in this manner.
Instruct the patient to place their head in your lap, and have an assistant hold their head with both hands so that it does not move or shake.
Then apply a cautery with the shape like this to the eye after placing a poultice of infused cotton in the membrane of an egg or in slippery elm mucilage on it.
Let it be concave like the shape of a vulture's feather quill from one end, with which the cautery is made; and if you wish for it to penetrate to the other end, or if you wish for it to go upward, do so in this manner.
However, this concave shape is better suited for your task.
Then squeeze out the pus if it is open, and extract the pus from it, and dry it; and if it is not open, then open it and extract its pus.
Then apply a very hot cautery to it.
And hold your hand with the cautery near the eye towards the side of the nose so that your hand does not wander or disturb the patient; and place the cautery on the fat of the eye and destroy it.
If you reach with your cautery to the bone at its beginning, it will be good. And if not, then repeat the cautery once or twice, if you need it; and leave it for three days.
Then apply a cotton poultice with butter, and treat him with drying ointment until he is healed.
But if forty days pass and he is not healed, then apply a sharp corrosive medicine to him until the bone is exposed; and scrape it according to its chapter.
And there is another method for cauterizing a fistula that some of the first [surgeons] have said. And you should place over the sick person's eye a cloth soaked in egg white or water.
For lead burns away the site of the fistula and heals it with remarkable healing.
If the fistula is healed along with what we have said about cautery and treatment, it is good. And if not, then it is necessary to administer the nasal passage and lead the fistula into the course of the nose, so that it will come to its own proper place.

"On the method of cauterizing the stomach.

"And space them apart so that they do not join together when producing pus.
"And let the depth of the cautery be two-thirds the thickness of the skin.
"And let the shape of the cauteries be according to this pattern without addition. And if you wish, cauterize with a large cautery in the middle of the stomach according to this pattern. "On the method of cauterizing a cold liver.

And let the amount that is burned be from the thickness of the skin, and let it be half of its amount not added; and let the patient stand on his feet.

Â¶ On the method of cauterizing liver abscesses.
When an abscess occurs and you wish to know whether it is in the liver or its covering: then if it is in the liver itself, pain and heaviness come upon the patient without sharpness; but if it is in the covering of the liver, there is a very sharp pain along with it. And you will see that its treatment has exhausted its physicians.
Therefore, the patient should recline on his back. Then outline the site of the abscess with a caustic; then heat the cautery that resembles a ray. And this is its form. And burn with it one cautery until the entire skin is burned and reaches the vein, until all the pus comes out; then treat him with the treatment of abscesses until he is healed.
And it is not fitting that one use this type of cautery unless his study in the medical art is prolonged; and through whose hands these diseases have run their course with experience many times; then he may dare to undertake such an operation.
To dismiss it altogether is better in my opinion.
On the method of cauterizing in pleurisy.
The ancients said to use the cautery with the roots of Aristolochia for cold pleurisy in this manner. And it is that you should take from the dried, long roots of Aristolochia one root longer than any other, and let it be as thick as a finger. Then immerse it in oil and light it on fire. Then cauterize with one cautery on the place that is between the continuation of the collarbone and the neck, and with two small cauteries somewhat sloping towards the area under the chin.
And also with two cauteries on the place that is between the fifth and sixth ribs, sloping somewhat towards the back; and with another cautery in the middle of the chest, and another above the stomach. xspace And with three cauteries from behind: one on the place that is between the two shoulder blades; and two cauteries from both sides of the chest, below the cautery that is between the two shoulder blades.
And it is not necessary to press with your hand while using the cautery, but let it be freely sensed by the skin.
And some of the ancients said that there are men who use a cautery made of iron similar to a rod; they ignite it and insert it into the intercostal space until it reaches the abscess, and pus comes out, as we have said in the case of liver abscess. â™¡
But in this puncture with the cautery there is fear that either the patient dies immediately or a fistula occurs in that place which cannot be healed.

Then insert the two heated prongs until you pierce through to the other side of the skin; then remove the iron. Thus, four cauteries are made.
If you wish to cauterize with another iron having three prongs.

Â§ The Method of Cauterizing an Anal Fistula
Chapter XXXVIII
When the patient does not respond to incision and the operation we have described in its proper place, and is afraid of it, perhaps he can be cured with a cautery.
When therefore someone has an anal fistula and it is old, foul-smelling pus runs from it, and the place becomes corrupt. It is more fitting to do what is necessary: test it with a fine probe. Then learn the depth of its extent with the probe.
Then heat a cautery that is similar to a ray. ðŸ˜Š Then insert the heated cautery into the fistula itself and also as much of its length as the probe had entered.
And repeat the cautery over it until all the corrupted matter is burned away, once, or twice, or thrice, according to your need.
And guard against burning a nerve or large vein if it is there; or if the fistula extends to the body of the bladder or the body of the intestine, then avoid all these places.
And do not do this unless the fistula is in a fleshy place and you consider that it does not penetrate deeply.
Then care for the place until it heals.
But if the place closes and materials are cut off from it and it remains thus for a long time, then you should know that it has been completely healed. ðŸ˜Š
And if materials are not cut off from it, then you should know that it is deep-seated or there is a corrupted opening at its depth, or something similar to this, whose description will come in its place.

Â¶ On the way to cauterize sciatica.
When pain occurs in the small box of Anchae and its cause is cold and moisture; and when the patient is treated with what we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help and grows old; then it is necessary to free the patient from gross humors with fetid pills or with artificial pills and similar ones. â€Œ Then cauterize him.
And the way of cautery in it is according to two methods: either with a cautery and drying medicines, or with a cautery and fire. â€Œ â€Œ
A cautery with fire is according to many methods.
One of which is that you cauterize over the small box of Anchae with three triangular cauteries in this form. And make their depth either good or bad. And let the space that is between each cautery be as thick as a finger; and let the cautery be an olive oil one. â€Œ â€Œ

And burn away the thickness of the skin throughout.
This is a method for cautery in sciatica when the pain clings to the hip itself and does not extend to the thigh and leg.
But if it extends to the thigh and leg, then cauterize with two cauteries on the hip, over the place where the patient indicates the pain is, and your cautery four fingers below the iliac crest towards the flank a little: and let the cautery be of the knife type.
And let the depth of the cautery be according to the thickness of the skin.
But if the patient indicates that the pain extends almost to the toes, then cauterize him there where he indicates with a cautery of a point or three, or four, or more, if he needs it.
And if he indicates that the pain is under the knee towards the leg, then cauterize him there with one knife-type cautery.
And be careful in all your cautery not to go so far with the cautery that you burn a nerve or a large artery and draw upon the patient bad damage or contraction.
And I have indeed seen one and another of those who cauterized above the iliac crest and went too far in cautery, until the leg swelled up so that a tumor reached the foot, and the whole foot was perforated and rotted away; then there followed dissolution of the belly, and death after that.  ()
If the pain is in both parts at once, cauterize each according to this manner.
And some wise men have said concerning the cautery of the hip, which this method describes. Make a similar needle of iron, whose diameter is half the palm: and let it be at its opening according to the thickness of a nut-sized finger or a little less; and inside that needle, let there be another needle, one third in size.
And let there be a space between each needle the size of a thumb's knuckle; and let the needles be open from both ends; and let their height be like a knuckle, or two knuckles; and make for them a handle from iron, fittingly placed in the needles.
Then let it be heated in the fire until it turns red and throws off sparks; then place it on a jar of anchoise oil on the weak side where the healthy side is. Cauterize him, therefore, with three circular cauteries in one go.
Then leave him for three days. After that, apply plasters with butter; and leave the wound open for many days. Then care for him with ointment until he is healed.
Said Albucasis: "O my son, we have used this kind of cautery little, because of the terror of its appearance; and also, because we have found few who would endure it.
Nevertheless, it is one of the good cauteries for those who can bear it and find its place with it.
The cautery with burning medicines is done like this: make two needles with a perforated ring, into which descends the pin of its door made of bronze or iron, the length of the wall; in their height let there be two knuckles, or almost so.
And let there be a space between the two needles the size of a finger's thickness; and let them be open below and above; and let what they contain hold together according to this form.
Then place it on a jar of anchoise oil, with the patient lying weakly on the healthy side. And press your hand firmly over the jar of anchoise oil. Then pour between the two circles hot water, which has been heated a little with fire, and hold it for an hour; and let the patient bear its gnawing and burning, for he finds the gnawing like fire, until the gnawing stops.
Then raise your hand with the instrument and wash away the hot water from the whole wound with sweet water; then leave it for three days.
And put butter on it until the blackness of the burning is removed; and leave it for some days, and pus will flow from it. For it is the last resort in aid.
Then care for it with ointments until it heals.
If the pain extends as far as the hip or leg: make for him a container that holds water, according to what you did for the wound equally.
And this is the way of hot water; and I have already written about it in the treatise on the correction of drugs. Take alkali and unslaked lime, one part of each; grind both and put them in a new pot, the lower part of which has been pierced with a small hole through which the radius can pass. And place beneath the bottom of the pot another glass pot, and pour over the alkali and lime sweet water so that it covers both by one finger's width; after which you press them together with your hand using good pressure; and leave the pot until the sharp water descends to the lower part of the glass pot. )))
Then gather all that water and pour it over more lime; and boil until it is dissolved again.
For then it will be very strong in acuity, which is used in many operations of medicine and in the cautery of other members. Because it produces the effect of fire itself. )))
And among the medicines with which wounds are also cauterized, as with terebinth, and honey of the pistachio nut, and lime with soap, so that each is mixed together.
And Galen indeed related the treatment of some ancient man by which his pain in the wound and the sciatic vein was cured; and he said it was very effective. He said that no other treatment was needed, and that he was healed in one visit, until he returned and said that perhaps he had entered the bath carried by others, and came out of it already cured.
It should be taken from green seitan: and if it is not found fresh, let it be taken dry, recent; and let it be ground very much with some fat, and placed on the sore, whether it is on the leg or hip; and let it be bound, and left for three hours, or however long the patient feels a relief from the burn. Then put him in the bath.
Therefore, when his body becomes moist, put him into a chair. For the pain recedes and he is cured.
And know that no one should use cautery with these medicines except after the evacuation of the body.
And Dioscorides said that goat droppings, when used to cauterize the sciatic vein, are beneficial for it; and the cautery is made in this way. Take wool and soak it in old oil, and place it on the deep place which is between the big toe and the little finger of the foot, closer to the little finger.
Then take dry goat droppings and burn them in a fire until they become charcoal.
Then place the charcoal on the wool, and leave it until it is extinguished. Then repeat that process. Therefore, do not stop doing this until the pain is relieved all the way to the sore and the pain ceases.
And this method of cautery is called the cow's cautery.
Â¶ Concerning the cauterization of back pain.
Sometimes back pain occurs from many causes, either by accident or by a blow, or excessive evacuation, and similar things, due to the influx of cold and wet material; and cautery is only suitable for this kind alone, which comes about through the influx of cold material.
It is necessary after the evacuation of the patient with fetid pills and similar ones, that they be made on the back where there is pain, three lines according to the width of the ruler itself, after you mark with a cautery in every line five burns, or more according to the quantity that comes from the strength of the patient: and let the cauterization be done with a small puncture.
And if you wish, cauterize with three or four cauteries using a medium-sized cautery in this manner.
Concerning the method of cauterizing an unripe swelling.
This illness often happens to small children.
And the sign of its beginning in children is that they experience a constriction in their breath when lifted or moved, and the swelling is found at the end of the spine of the back and it already begins to protrude above the other vertebrae.
Therefore, when you see this and wish to treat it, then cauterize with a circular cautery in this manner.
And let the cautery be placed over all parts of the vertebrae equally; and if you wish, cauterize around the vertebra with a puncture cautery in two or three lines, and let the points be close to each other. xspace
Then care for the place until it is healed with what we have said.
And beware not to administer a cautery on a swelling that occurs from a spasm of the nerve.
Concerning the method of cauterizing gout and joint pains.
When the pains of the joints are from cold humors that flow to any member of the body, then when these pains occur in the feet, it is customary among doctors to name this specifically gout. xspace
When, therefore, gout of cold cause is being treated with methods of healing, and the pains are not removed, then cautery will remove them.
And it is as if you should cauterize him after evacuation around the joint of the foot with many cauteries, and let the cautery be of olive oil.
And if you need to prick on the sole of the foot, then do so with a pricking iron. If the pains ascend to the knees or other joints, and this often happens, then cauterize him on every knee with three or four cauteries from all sides with the same burning iron.
But if you need more of this cautery, then cauterize him with it. And do not dip your hand with the cautery into (the oil), but let it be approximately as thick as the skin.
But if the pains ascend to the knees and back, then administer what we have said about the cautery in its chapter.  (The "chapter" referred to here is likely the section of Albucasis's textbook that deals with treating these specific ailments.)
But if the pains are only in the hands, then prick around the fingers as two lines wrap around.
But if any pain remains in the fingers, then prick each one on every joint and on the palm of the hand.
But if the pains ascend after days to the elbows or shoulders, then cauterize both from every side.
And do not evacuate the sick person with a good diet or reception of medicines. For if the diet is good and the phlegm is evacuated, he will be cured with God's help along with this cautery.
Â¶ On the way of cauterizing a hernia.
When a hernia occurs in the groin, and an intestine or testicle descends to the testicle, and this is the first occurrence, it is necessary that you order the sick person to fast on that day.  (Here, "dimittere comestionem" means "to let go of food," i.e., to fast.) And let him use laxatives so that his feces may descend from his belly.
Then have him sit between your hands on his back; and instruct him to hold his breath until the feces or a piece of intestine comes out.
Then bring him back with your fingers, and mark with caustic on the rupture above the pubis, with a mark whose end is similar to half of a circle, towards the upper part of the body.
Then heat the caustic until it turns white and ejects sparks. Then return the intestine or feces to its proper place. Then have the assistant place his hand over the site so that the intestine does not come out; and you have already made an incision between the patient's thighs, and placed a pillow beneath him, and another servant is sitting on his thighs, and another on his chest to hold his hands.  />
Then place the caustic over that mark, with your hand holding the caustic upright. And hold him until you reach the orifice with it; or repeat the process again if you do not reach the orifice on the first attempt.
And carefully observe the exit of the intestine during your use of the caustic, lest you burn it, and cause death or great harm to the patient.
And know that when you do not reach the orifice with the caustic, your operation is of no benefit.
And it is necessary for the caustic to be fine and subtle, according to their size.
Then care for him with other ointments until he is healed.
And let the patient lie on his back for forty days, until the wound closes.
And it is necessary that you give him food during the time of his treatment, which will soften his belly so that the intestine does not come out during defecation and evacuation.
Then, when he wants to get up after forty days, administer a well-made bandage, and let him hold it for another forty days.
And he should be kept from work, and from excessive food and drink, and from loud voices.
For when he uses this treatment plan, he is cured with complete healing.
And I will say the treatment of ruptures with incision in its own chapter.
But when ruptures occur in the rest of the belly and are beginning, and you want to prevent them from getting worse, then cauterize the rupture with a round cautery according to its size: and let what is burned be one third of it. Then treat him as we have said: and it will not get worse.
And some of the earlier authors said that the rupture should be cauterized with a triangular cautery, according to this shape.
After it is marked with wax and a line is placed which is the width across the top of the rupture, and another line below it. And place your hand in the middle with a pointed cautery.
But the first cautery is easier and better.
Â¶ On the method of cauterizing for pain due to a fall or blow.
Chapter 48
When pain occurs in some members from a fall or blow and that pain persists for a long time and does not improve with medical treatment, then it is necessary to cauterize with a pointed cautery.
And the cautery of every member should be according to its size and thinness and weakness and strength and the place where the blow struck and caused pain from it. bey
If he is then cured by the first cautery, that is good. If not, then repeat the cautery on him. bey
For it is customary for these pains to be transferred from one member to the nearest one. Therefore, you must use the cautery on them until the patient heals.
Â¶ On Cauterizing for Leprosy
Sometimes, lepers are greatly helped by the aid of the cautery. And especially the kind of leprosy that occurs due to the putrefaction of phlegm and black bile; when you wish to cauterize it, take this into consideration.
If the leprosy is at its beginning and you have treated it with what we said in the division, but it does not descend or stay; and you fear for the patient that corruption may spread over his whole constitution, then cauterize him on five points on the head: one in the middle of the forehead, another below it towards the front, at the end of the hairline; two on the two temples; and one at the back of the neck.
And finally, hold the cautery briefly in your hand until it leaves a small impression on the skin, and the scales are loosened from there; so that the exhalation of thick vapors is relieved, and also cauterize the spleen with the cautery, as we mentioned before. Â•
But if the leprosy is already spread over the patient and clearly appears; then you should cauterize with these cauteries that we mentioned on the head, and one cautery on the tip of the nose, and two on each cheek, and two on each vertebra of the neck, and six on each vertebra of the back, and a large one on the groin at the base of the tail and one above it in the anus; and two on each shoulder blade; that is, one on each entire shoulder blade, and two on each knee; one on each entire knee, and two on each elbow, and two on each wrist, and two on each tender part of his chest. And you should cauterize him on every joint of the fingers of his hands and feet; and cauterize on each heel of his feet and the palms of his hands.
And beware of the nerves that are above the lower part of the heel, so that you do not burn them.
And sometimes it is cauterized with a cautery on the top of the pubic bone, and another on the top of the stomach, and another on the liver.
And know that the more you apply the cautery, it is a greater help and more beneficial.
And know that the sick person does not find pain in the cautery as the healthy person finds it: because his body is already numb.
And the cauteries should be of appropriate size and shape according to the members and joints: as was previously said concerning the types of instruments.
Then take care of the cauteries with a paste made from herbs and honey, and continue the treatment until it heals.
Â¶ On the Method of Cauterizing in Coma.
When any member is in a coma and is treated with medicines, oils, and plasters, but does not heal, then cauterize the comatose member with cauteries, according to the size or shape of the member.
And let your cautery penetrate into the thickness of the skin a little bit. Then take care of it with an ointment until it heals.
And sometimes it is cauterized for a certain type of coma that affects the hand or foot, in the joints of the back at the point where the nerves that move that member exit: and the coma will be removed.
But do not attempt this unless you are skilled in the anatomy of the members and the exit of the nerves that move the body. ]{
Chapter LI
When leprosy is longstanding and nothing helps from the skills of medicine: then cauterize with a deep cautery briefly, according to the thickness of the skin, until the whiteness is removed and its color changes.
Then care for it with a herb and lentil flour mixed with rose oil, and arnoglossa leaves, and the blood of a dove, and the blood of a swallow: let there be an equal part of each; all these are to be mixed together and spread on a cloth, and applied to the place, until it heals.
About the method of cautery for cancer.
When the cancer is beginning and you wish to stop it, then cauterize it with a circular cautery all around it as it is turning.
The wise men have said that it should be cauterized in the middle with the last cautery.
But this does not seem right to me, because I fear that it will cause an ulcer; and indeed I have seen this happen many times. Â¶ Deinde cauteriza ipsum cum cauterio ultimo in circuitu eius sicuti reuoluitur.
And it is better that it be cauterized around its circumference with a circle, as we have said, or with many small cauteries.
About the method of cautery for adubelatis (a type of abscess or boil).
When someone has an adubelatis and it is delayed in coming to a head, either because of an excess of fluid that causes it, or because the patient is old and weak with little blood, or because of the time and you wish to hasten the maturation of the adubelatis, then cauterize around its circumference with many small punctures. Then leave it alone. For it will hasten in its maturation.
But if you wish to pierce it with a cautery, then heat the cautery, which has this shape:
And place it in the middle of the adubelatis until it penetrates the skin. The cautery should be made by the infirmarius so that he may lighten the course of the pus.
Then care for it until it heals.
In the manner of cauterizing in a malignant ulcer.
Chapter 44.
A corrosive ulcer is nothing but a corruption walking through the body, and it eats away at it, just as fire consumes dry wood.
Therefore, if you see a corrosive ulcer in a place that can tolerate cautery with fire, then use much fire cautery, both small and large needles, according to what is suitable for the place where the corrosion is located.
Then cauterize it on all sides until you have completely eradicated the entire corruption, and nothing remains of it whatsoever. xspace
Then leave it alone for three days and place powdered sulfur mixed with oil on the cauterized places until all the scabs are removed, and all corruption is eliminated.
Then care for it with flesh-generating ointments.
If, therefore, you see that after three days healthy flesh is generated, in which there is no corruption, it is good.
And if not: then repeat the cautery on what remains of the corrupted places.
And the corrosive ulcer is treated sometimes with sharp medicine. For it arises in the place of cautery.
However, cautery with fire is a faster remedy, and I have already mentioned its cauterization with sharp medicine in the division; take it there when you need it.
In the manner of cauterizing warts and verrucas.
Chapter 50.
Often this disease occurs in the lower parts of the feet; it is a thick, fibrous growth that injures the foot.
And there are two types of cautery for them: cautery with fire and cautery with hot water. xbspace xthe first is performed as follows: take some sulfur and mix it with the oil of violets and make a small needle from it, and apply it to the wart or verruca. xthen light the needle with a flame until it becomes very hot, and then place it on the wart or verruca. xthen continue heating it until it sticks to it like wax, and when you have done this, leave it in place for a while until it cools down.
"As for that which is with fire, burn a hollow cautery like the feather of a vulture: let it be made of iron, according to the size that contains a nail from all sides; and let it have fine edges.
"Then place the burning one on top of the nail. "Then turn the hand with the cautery around the nail until it reaches the depth of the nail; and leave it for three days until it begins to emit pus. "Then apply a plaster on it with wild mallows crushed with salt; and leave the plaster on it at night. "It will indeed be rooted out from its roots.
"Then treat the place with a regenerative flesh ointment until it heals.
"But if they do not turn, and often happen on the surface of the body, especially in hands and feet; then apply a cautery with hot water to them: and it is done by taking a tube made of bronze, or iron, or from a vulture's feather; and place it on the nail or wart."  /> "Then pour a small amount of hot water into the tube; hold your hand, and turn it with the pressure of your hand for a moment, so that the edge of the tube is imprinted on the root of the nail, and let the hot water find a path to the depth, to the root of the nail: and let the patient wait briefly over the stinging of the hot water for one hour.
"Then leave it alone, for the nail will be rooted out with its roots.
"Do this one after another until you have treated all that are on the body.
"Then treat them afterward with whatever ointments regenerate flesh.
"On the method of cauterizing in tremors.
When someone experiences a tremor due to cold in the nerve, or from tertian fever, or for some other reason, then it is necessary to cauterize them with four or five cauteries on the spinal column of the back, and between every vertebrae one cautery, and one cautery on their chest, and one on their stomach.
For the tremor subsides with cautery of olive oil, and health is hastened from cold sickness.
About the method of cauterizing by Albucasis.
Chapter 57
Sometimes foul things are expelled from the body by Albucasis's method, namely pustules which form from heavy, rotten matter.
Therefore, as soon as they appear, they should be cauterized over the top of every pustule with a fine cautery using lit myrtle wood whose tip is set on fire. Or with a long root of birthwort. Or with a lentil-shaped cautery. xspace
And sometimes they are cauterized with a burner at the beginning of their expulsion in this way, and they do not increase; the excess causing them is broken up, and healing comes from them.
However, it should be done after evacuation with bloodletting.
About the method of cauterizing for bleeding from an artery in a wound.
It often happens that there is bleeding from an artery which has been cut in a wound, whether it occurs externally or at the incision of an aposteme or member's cautery, and similar things; and it is difficult to stop it. ï¸Ž â€Œ
When this happens to someone, then quickly place your hand on the opening of the artery and put your index finger over it; and press hard until the blood is blocked under your finger and nothing comes out from it.
Then place a small cauterizing instrument made of iron into the fire and several large ones; blow on them until they become very hot.
Then take one of the instruments, either small or large, according to the wound and the place where the artery has been cut; quickly remove your finger and place the cautery on the vein itself, and hold it there until the blood is cut off.
But if it is driven out along with the elevation of your finger from the opening of the artery, and you extinguish the cautery, then quickly take another cautery from those that are prepared in the fire.
Do not therefore cease to do this with one after another until the blood is cut off.
And be careful not to burn the nerve that is there, lest something else happen to the patient.
And know that when blood flows from the artery, then it is not possible to cut it off; especially when the artery is large, unless with one of four methods. Or with a cautery, as we have said. Or with extraction, when it has not been extracted. For when it is extracted, its ends contract, and the blood is cut off. â†‘ Or it may be tied with a strong thread of binding. Or medicines that have the property of cutting off blood may be placed on it and tied tightly with a decent compress.
However, he who cuts it off with a ligature and constriction with a cloth or with the application of burning substances and such does not help at all, except rarely.
But if this happens to someone and there is no physician present or medicine; then let him begin with the position of his index finger on the opening of that vein, as we have described, and with its very tight constriction, until the blood is held back from the upper part of the wound and above the artery. â†‘ And the finger should not be moved; pour cold water of intense cold over it until the blood freezes and thickens, and is cut off.
And during that time he should consider whether anything is needed from the cautery or medicine.
Concerning the incision, puncturing, and venesection in wounds and similar cases.
As we have said in the first chapter, every illness that is suitable for the use of the cautery and burning medicine, along with its causes, instruments, and types of cautery.
And I placed there chapters from the head down to the feet.
And I will proceed in this chapter along the same path, so that what is sought may be clear to those who seek it.  />
And before I begin that, it is necessary for you, O sons, to learn what is in this chapter from fear of what is in the first chapter about cautery.
And because of this, greater care is necessary, for in the operation that is in this chapter, there often occurs an evacuation with blood, with which life stands at the opening of a vein, or an incision over an abscess, or the opening of a fistula, or the treatment of a wound, or the extraction of an arrow, or an incision over a stone, and similar things: from all these comes trembling, fear, and in many of them death occurs.  />  />  >
And I warn you that this hesitation does not fall upon you, for sometimes people with various conditions come to you in this art. For among them is one who becomes angry with his illness, and death is light for him because of the severity he finds from his illness and its long-standing evil.  />  />  >  /> "And with illness from fear which signifies death.
"And among them is one who gives his flute to you and enriches you with it, hoping for health, but his illness is deadly.
"Therefore, you should not agree with him who comes to you from among them, whose manner is such. "And let your caution be greater than your greed and your rapacity. "And do not assume anything from him unless after certain knowledge, which verifies for you the praiseworthy outcome to which he has arrived.
"And use in the treatment of all your sick, prognosis and diagnosis for that to which health is properly suited.
"In this indeed you have assistance in the acquisition of fame and glory, and memory and praise.
"May God inspire you, O sons, with his understanding, and may he not take away your guidance and inspiration, for that is in his hand.
