Chapter 82
You should know that Almirmar is nothing but a round knot according to the color of the body, similar to the head of a nail: and it occurs throughout the body, especially in the lower parts of the feet and toes; and from this comes pain during walking.
Therefore, it must be cut around the head of the nail and held with forceps or a hook, and it should be pulled out from its root.
Then care for it: and if you wish, cauterize it according to what has been said previously in its chapter.
From athalil, however, there is one small rough, crusty, round lump above the surface of the body. And they often occur in children's hands.
And its treatment is that you stretch the athalil and cut it off: or tie it with a silk thread: or with hair, until it falls off. And if you wish, cauterize it with fire or sharp medicine as previously mentioned: and thus the inverted athalils, and not the uninverted ones, are removed with an instrument that I will mention.
However, a formica is also a small rough lump on the surface of the body, going very deep: and when it encounters cold, it feels like an ant bite, and it occurs throughout the body: and it mostly happens in hands.
And its treatment is that you take a quill from a goose feather or a strong vulture feather: and place this quill over the formica, until the circle of the quill contains its parts. Then turn your hand with the quill until you cut what is around the formica: and place it deep into the flesh, and pull out the formica from its root.
And if you wish, do this with a quill of brass or iron, in this shape.

Chapter 83
"Concerning the shapes of instruments that are used for enemas in cases of illnesses of the anus and to relieve the intestines and colic.
"Sometimes an enema is made of silver, or copper, or cast bronze, or hammered.
"And sometimes these instruments are made small and large according to those into whom they are administered.
"Therefore, that which is administered for the treatment of small children should be small; and likewise their enemas if their anus is weak or painful.
"A large enema.
"The tube of it, that is, the upper end where the bag is tied, should be wide according to this manner; and there should be a distinct part so that the bag can be tied as you see, and its lower end which enters into the anus should be plugged, that is, not open, very gentle, drawing to fineness; and on one of its sides there should be two holes, and on the other side one hole.
"And the width of the hole should be according to the thickness of the reeds, somewhat thicker; and let the bag in which the medicines are placed be from a bladder of an animal or from sheepskin, which should be according to the shape of a small syringe, whose tube is one palm long.
"And it should be pierced with many holes as it is rolled, and the space between each hole should be the thickness of a finger. "Then insert through those holes a thread made of raw silk, which should consist of ten threads or thereabouts, and attach the bag to it like an ear syringe. When therefore it is placed within, let the enema be tied at the head between two tightenings with a strong constriction. Then let him be given an enema with it.
And this is the form of the circle of the bag here depicted, and its openings.
The quality of administering the enema with it is this: that you fill the bag or bladder with medicine which has been heated according to the tolerance of the patient; and be careful that it is not very hot nor very cold.
Then let the patient be turned onto their back and lift up their legs; and place under him an intahaan, that is, a hide upon which people lie, or a cloth.
Then anoint the end of the enema with oil, or with egg white, or with fenugreek mucilage, or similar substances. Then insert it into the anus gently. Then let the attendant take the bag with both his hands together and squeeze it forcefully until he has expelled all that is within the enema into the intestine.
Then remove the enema, and let the patient raise their legs against the wall.
And if the medicine forces him to go out, then let him hold it as long as he is able. And if he sleeps with it throughout the night, it is more efficacious in its assistance.
But if you give him an enema for abdominal pains and his evacuation is urgent; then repeat the enema until he is cured.
And if there are hemorrhoids or painful abscesses in the anus, then let the enema be very fine and mild, like those with which children are given enemas.
And this is the form of a fine enema on which the skin should be tightly drawn.
Chapter 84
And I have already said in the division on the treatment of wounds what was suitable for the book, and here I will say the treatment of them with the hand and with medicines according to their nature.
Therefore, I say that wounds are distinguished according to that by which the wound is made and according to the place upon which the wound falls.
The things by which wounds are made are often like these: a blow with a stone; or a cut with a sword or knife; or a strike with a spear, stick, or arrow; and similar things from many objects.
Moreover, wounds according to the parts of the body are as follows: a wound that falls upon the head, or neck, or chest, or belly, or liver; and similar things from those members.
And I am narrating the treatments of some wounds so that I may place this reasoning and rule over other wounds. ã€‹
And I will begin with simple head wounds, because the treatment of compound wounds will come at the beginning of the third chapter.
Therefore, I say. When a simple wound occurs on the head and there is no fracture of bone, consider if it is from the blow of a stone or similar things and has only torn the skin, and the wound is large, and you fear an unfavorable outcome of a hot aposteme; then hasten and make an immediate cephalic phlebotomy; and do not delay that; and draw out from the blood according to its quantity. If there is nothing preventing the phlebotomy, especially if the amount of blood coming out of the wound is small. And let the phlebotomy be from the opposite side of the wounded part.
And let the phlebotomy be from the opposite side of the wounded part. And let the patient take care to avoid fullness, and wine, and heavy foods.
If something prevents the cutting off, then let it be cut off from food, and not approach meats or wines.
And place on the wound if it develops a hot abscess, cooked onion infused only in rose oil or with wine that has an astringent property.
But if you are safe from the hot abscess, then place on the wound, if it is fresh with its own blood and the air has not changed it, the powder that I will describe shortly: and if the air has already changed it, then place on it certain ointments until it heals.
But if the wound is large or from a sword cut and similar: and its edges do not come together with stitches, then gather them with stitching, as I will describe in the chapter on wounds of the belly about their stitching.
But if the wound has already been detached from the bone and hangs down and there is no retention of it except in a small ligament: then cut it off. Then care for the wound with medicines and restore hard flesh in place of skin, and instruct the patient to be nourished with foods that are thick like porridge and boiled wheat until it is like a paste and similar foods.
But if you find putrefaction in the skin and it does not adhere to the bone, then cut off all of the putrefied part and throw it away; then care for it.
But if in these wounds there is an artery or vein from which blood flows and it does not clot with medicines, then seek for the artery. Therefore if you find it uncut, then cut it with a scalpel or ligature it. But if necessity demands when the aforementioned method does not work, then cauterize it until the blood clots.
If these wounds are small and simple, then their condition is easy and light; sprinkle this powder over them, for it will heal them before the air changes them.
Method of the flesh-forming powder: Take one part of frankincense and two parts of dragon's blood, and three parts of fresh lime. Grind them all together very finely and sift them; then fill the wound with it and bind it tightly until it adheres well and coagulates with the blood.
Then bind it over with small pieces of cloth, and leave it undisturbed until it is completely healed, so that it does not become detached. For the medicine will not be removed from it until it has healed.
And sometimes lime alone does this, when you do not have frankincense and dragon's blood at hand; for dragon's blood also performs the same function in many large wounds, when it is placed upon them and they are bound, and the wounds are fresh with their own blood, which the air has not yet changed.
But if the air has already changed them somewhat, especially in summertime, then this powder is not useful for their treatment; therefore care for them with what we have said, placing upon them certain digestive ointments, or place upon them poultices made from barley meal, mixed with water and honey, until they put forth pus. Then care for them with the remaining treatment until they are healed.
But if a bone is broken along with the wound, and it is small, then extract it with pincers; and now I will speak of the treatment for head fractures as follows.
On wounds of the neck:
But if a wound occurs on the neck, there is no difference in its treatment from that of a simple head wound.
If however the nerve of the neck or artery has already been cut: then if it is a nerve, there is no remedy for it, except to avoid its treatment with what causes intense coagulation, such as ziniar and zegi, and similar things. Since they harm nerves and constrict them.
And you shall not place anything cold at all on the wound; because the substance of nerves is cold, and its continuation is with the brain, which is the highest part of the body: and let that which is used for treatment be mild, such as lime washed many times with sweet water mixed with oil, or with rose oil and tuthia, when it is also washed with sweet water; and other mineral stones in this manner, and moist ointments.
However, if the wound is large, then apply stitches; or close its lips with small pieces of cloth. Then care for him until he heals.
However, if the wound is deep or an abscess has formed at its lower part where pus is already gathering, then pierce it in a deeper place therein.
If an artery has been cut in the wound and its bleeding has followed, then separate it or cut it off and tie it; or cauterize it if necessity demands that.
However, if the thyroid cartilage has been cut entirely or in part and the alhaudaj have been saved, then gather the lips of the skin with stitches above the cricoid cartilage, and do not touch the throat; rather make it equal and return it to its natural shape. Then bind it with a proper tightness and leave it for several days. Then care for him with ointments that have coagulant and drying properties until he heals.
If the wound has already made an impression on the bone, then examine it: if there are bone fragments in it, remove all of them, or as many as you can; and what is not ready, leave it until the wound becomes putrid, and its opening separates and softens.
If the wound is fresh, then sprinkle on it the powder that I mentioned. If bone appears in the wound and a fistula forms, then treat it as mentioned in its chapter.
Â¶ On wounds of the lips.
If it is a wound from a spear or knife: and you see its depth, then observe. If, therefore, there is windiness coming out of the wound when the patient pants, then know that the wound is mortal.
But if the wound is not deep and it is fresh with its own blood: then do not put powder on it from the first hour, nor bind it, so that the blood is not retained in its depth and returns to the heart and kills the patient; but put on it a drawing ointment, and dissolve it twice a day.
But if you do not have the ointment present, then put an old cloth on the mouth of the wound to absorb what comes out of it from moisture; and make the patient sleep on the wound so that what accumulates in it runs off.
But if three days or more have already passed for the wound, and no spasm, nor bad heart tremor, nor constriction in breathing has befallen the patient, and you see that its other dispositions are good: then know that the wound is safe. Therefore, treat him with linen cloths and the rest of the treatment until he is healed.
If healing is hindered and it always opens up again, then know that a fistula has formed. Treat it according to its own chapter.
And if the wound is from the cut of a sword or knife and is simple on the surface of the chest or back, then treat it with what was mentioned before for stitching, if it is large; or with powder, if it is small.
But if it has already made an imprint on the bone and fragments have broken off from it, then search for the wound and hasten to extract those fragments if they are separate. But if they are not separate, then leave them until the wound becomes foul, for their extraction will be easier.
But the treatment of other wounds occurring in other parts follows the same judgment as we said.
Â¶ On Wounds of the Belly and Exit of Intestines and Their Healing
A wound that occurs in the belly is great, medium, or small.
Therefore, from a great wound sometimes an intestine or several intestines protrude.
Because of this, their introduction and their stitching are more forceful and difficult.
And a small wound also becomes difficult in another way. Therefore, if you do not hasten to return them immediately to their place, the swelling will occur, it will open up and become thick, which makes their entry difficult.
Therefore, a medium wound is better for wounds, because with it the return of the intestine is not difficult, as it happens with these two kinds.
Know that the stitching of the belly is in four ways.
Two stitches are common to the stitching of the belly and to the stitching of other wounds of the body, while two other stitches are peculiar to other wounds.  /> > The common ones are: the first one is a simple one, and the second one is with a needle. Truly they are more specific for the closure of the abdomen: and I narrate each to you with explanation and elucidation.
I say therefore, that when the wound is small and some of the intestine has protruded from it, and it is difficult to reduce it, then this is because of one of two things. Either because of the smallness of the wound, as we said: Or because there is swelling in the intestine due to cold air.
Therefore, when this is the case, you should heat it so that you dip a sponge or wet cloth in warm water alone. Or boil in water safflower, cumin, and nutmeg, and smear the intestine with it until the swelling is resolved.
Sometimes he does this with wine that has astringency, and it is better than plain water for resolving swelling.
Therefore, when you see the swelling has been resolved, then moisten the intestine with water in which althea or mallow has been boiled. For through this its entry will be facilitated with something small. â€º
But if its return is hindered after this treatment, then find the small wound with an instrument used for cutting hemorrhoids.
And the first cure is better when it is prepared than when it is cut: and there is no need to cut after necessity and lack of an instrument.
Let one part of it be twisted and pointed, and the other part not pointed, and let its tip not be very fine like a spatula, but rather somewhat blunter; and it is similar to a hook, as you see. â€º â€º
Therefore, when the wound is enlarged and the intestine comes out, it is necessary that its reduction be according to its natural shape in its proper place, if possible, for this is better. â€º â€º
When however there is a large disruption in the lower part of the abdomen, then it is necessary that you make the patient lie on his back, and place his legs higher than his head. And if it is in the upper part of the abdomen, then place his head and chest higher than his lower parts.
And likewise if there is a disruption in one of the two parts of the abdomen, then direct your attention and your care always to this, that the part in which the wound is may be higher than the other part.
And thus you should do this for large wounds and medium wounds.
But for small wounds, place it as it is prepared for you.
Then make sure that there is a pious assistant at hand who holds the entire disruption with his hand: and gather its lips together. Â• Then let him who follows take the stitching one thing after another, and this is the common method of single stitching.
And it is that you should take a needle or a number of needles according to the size of the wound. Then leave from the end of the disruption a thumb's width, that is, the doctor's; and insert one needle through what you put in it a thread at both ends of the skin, with both ends of the sinew that is under the skin from within, until you make it penetrate on the other side, and you have already gathered together two ends of the skin and two ends of the sinew: and there are four rows.
Then pull with the double thread around the needle several times from both sides together, until the two lips of the wound are gathered together with a decent union.
Then leave another thumb's width, and insert another needle; afterwards draw it with the thread, as you did with the first needle. You should not hesitate to perform it with what you need from the cubits until you complete the constriction of the entire wound.
And let the needles be of medium size between thickness and thinness: for thin needles cut the flesh very quickly; and thick ones are difficult to enter into the skin; therefore, they ought to be of medium size in both thinness and thickness.
And it is not appropriate that the needle be inserted in the two extremities of the skin very close together so that the flesh is not cut quickly and the wound opens before its own healing, and also so that they do not elongate with the suture, lest the wound be prevented from healing.
Then cut the ends of the needles so that they do not harm the patient in his sleep; and put small woolen cloths around them from all sides, which hold the ends of the needles; and leave them there until you know that the wound has already healed.
And this type of suture with needles is more suitable for small wounds in this manner. Because one needle, or two, or about that number is sufficient for their suture.
However, the second type of suture is common, so that you gather with the suture the extremities of four: two extremities of skin and two silk threads in place of one, with a needle on which an equal thread is wound in thinness and thickness.
Then, when you have penetrated these four extremities with the needle, bring the needle back from the side where you began, so that the thread falls and remains at the upper part of the wound; thus let the suture be like the suture of a cloth by which clothes are sewn together. And put between each entire suture the thickness of a little finger.  />
This type of suture is known to people.
And with this suture I healed a man of the wound which had happened to him in his belly, who had been wounded with a knife; and there was a rupture of the wound greater than one palm: and about two palms of the middle intestine had come out, and the rupture was in the middle of the belly.  />  />
I therefore returned after his intestine protruded from the wound for twenty-four hours.
The wound was therefore healed after about fifteen days, and I treated it, and he was cured; and he lived many years afterward, converted to his own ways.
And the physicians judged that he would not be cured.
And it was a miracle that I did not treat it with an ointment. Because I was in a place where no ointment could be found, nor any medicine at all. I therefore placed an old cloth over the wound twice a day, and I continued to wash it with honey water until it was healed.
I will describe two proper types of suture according to the account of the text.
And it is that you begin with an acute suture: and you insert the needle from the outer part to the inner part.
Therefore, when the needle has penetrated the skin and into the flesh along the length and width of the entire body: leave the end of the thread on one side where you inserted the needle, and make it penetrate to the other end from the inner part to the outer part at the opposite end.
Therefore, when you have made it penetrate in this way at that end from the outer part to the inner part: leave the thread on this side, and make the needle penetrate into the other end from the inner part to the outer part; and with your penetration as you are making it penetrate into the thread at the opposite end, which is in its place, until it penetrates completely.  />
Then begin again from that same side, and bring it together with the end which is from the thread on the opposite side, and withdraw the needle from the skin which it had penetrated.  />
Then bring it back into that skin, and join the thread on one side with this end of the thread; and withdraw it from the skin which is on that side, and do this once and again; and continue to do this alternately, until you have brought everything together completely in this way.
And the essence of this stitch is like the stitches used by tanners to draw skins together; so that you should make a suture once from one end of the skin, and leave it in place on the other side, until you complete it.
The second type of proper stitch, which Galen called.
This is the narrative of its description, and it should be made similarly to how some physicians make it, so that they bring together every part with its fitting counterpart by nature: and they apply one end of the thread to the other end of it, and one end of the needle to the other end. And this is done according to what I tell you.
You should pierce the needle into the end of the thread nearest to you from the outside, and make it penetrate inside in this way only; and leave two ends of the thread. Then turn the needle and make it penetrate from the outside to the inside through both ends of the thread, that is, on both sides.
Then turn both and make them penetrate from the inside to the outside through the other two ends of the thread, which are on the opposite side.
And this method of stitching is better than the common easy one, and it is the stitch which was mentioned before.
This then is also the narrative of Galen.
And some said: The stitching of the belly is done with two needles.  /> That is, you insert one thread into both of them; and begin with the introduction of the needle from what is on your side, and make it penetrate to the other side according to the stitching of those who equally sew skins.
And know that when the rupture is in the middle of the belly, then its stitching is more difficult than in other places of the belly.
The judgment of a wound's treatment is the same as that for other wounds.
Because when you get a fresh wound with its own blood, before the air changes it: and bring out the intestines, and sew them up, and apply suitable remedies: then place powdered incense on it.
But if the air has already changed the wound, then place upon it certain ointments that you have at hand, until they produce pus; and the threads fall out, and the sutures (or stitches) strengthen, and heal (or close up). Then care for it as you would other wounds, until it heals.
But if the remedies are not at hand, then place upon it immediately, from when it begins to emit pus, old linen cloth: and change it twice a day, as I have taught you, until it heals.
For you do not need another treatment for most conditions when the wounds are simple (or straightforward).
But if you fear that the wound might communicate with the main parts (or vital organs) in an injury, then it is necessary to soak soft wool in moderately warm oil or rose oil: and place it around the areas between the groin and under the armpits.
If he feels pain or pangs or putrefaction in his bowels (for this often happens), then give him an enema with black, warm, astringent wine: especially if putrefaction has already reached the intestines and caused an exit wound through to its cavity.
And know that what comes from the large intestine is easier to heal: and what comes from the small (intestines) is more difficult to heal.
The intestine called the jejunum does not accept healing at all from a wound that occurs in it: and this is because of its great number of veins and their size, and because of the thinness of its body, and the closeness of its nature to the nerves (or nervous system).
If, however, that which comes out of the wound is the zirb (i.e., a piece of bowel), and you acquire it freshly: bring it back according to your reduction, by which you bring back the bowels equally.
If, however, the time has passed and it is now green or black, then it is necessary that you bind it with a thread above the place where it became darkened, so that there will not be a flow of blood. For in the zirb (i.e., piece of bowel) there are veins and arteries.
Then cut what is beyond that ligature and place the two ends of the thread hanging from below the wound outside it, so that its traction upon you may be relieved, and to prevent adhesion at the site of the bowel and emission of pus from the wound.
Â§ A reminder of a wound that occurs in the intestine.
When a disruption occurs in the intestine and it is small, then it is possible that it may be restored in some people; for I have seen someone who was wounded in his belly with the thrust of a spear, and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and the wound became old, and it formed a fistula, and from it came excretion and flatulence.
Therefore, I applied treatment until I was confident about his healing; nor did I cease to investigate him, until he was healed and the place was strengthened.
After I saw the place was already strengthened, I feared for the patient lest he suffer an accidental evil in his belly; and no accidental evil happened to him from that. â€º And he remained in his better condition, eating and drinking, having intercourse, and entering the bath, and he practiced his regular activities. â€º
And now some of the experimenters said that when a wound occurs in the intestine and it is small, then it ought to be tied up in this manner. And it is that you should take large-headed ants. Then bring together the two lips of the wound, and place one ant with its mouth open upon the two lips of the wound. When it bites into it, and closes its mouth, cut off its head; for it sticks there and does not come loose.
Then place another ant near the first one, and do not cease to do this with ants, one after another, according to the size of the whole wound.
Then bring it back, and let the wound close. For those heads remain attached within the intestine until the intestines have digested them and healed, and no harm comes to the patient at all.
And it is now possible to tie the intestine even with a fine thread; that is, what has been cleansed from the intestines of an animal and attached with it after it is inserted into the needle.
And it is that you should take the end of this thread from the intestine, and remove the flesh much. Then tie a fine, thin linen thread at its end. â‹… Then insert that thread into the needle, and sew with it along with the intestine. Then bring it back to its break.
And this method of suturing with ants and intestine is only according to the path of trust and hope.
Know that a large, wide wound, especially if it is in one of the thin intestines: then there is no remedy except for scraping away, and its healing does not happen at all.
Â¶ On the care of goiters and fistulas.
Know that every wound or abscess, when it becomes old and chronic, and turns into an ulcer, and does not heal, and always emits pus, and is not cut away: then it is universally called a fistula in whatever member it may be, and we call it Zuchemen.
And indeed a fistula is truly a hard, white, perforated swelling with no pain, having the concavity of a bird's feather; and because of this, some call it Risati, that is, feather.
And there are certain hours in which it becomes moist, emitting pus. And perhaps the moisture divides in certain hours. And sometimes this moisture is abundant, and sometimes scarce; it can be thick, or thin.
And I have already mentioned this in the division, when I said 'wounds', that every ulcer which does not heal and does not generate flesh is caused by one of nine causes.
One of these causes is either due to the scarcity of blood in the body, or its corruption; or because there is hard flesh between it and its lips, preventing the generation of flesh; or because it contains much dirt and filth; or because the ulcer itself is putrid and the substance sent to it is of poor quality; or because the medicine used for its treatment is unsuitable; or because the falling corruption in that region is of a pestilential nature, or due to a property of the region, as occurs in Caesaraugusta, where the digestion of diseases is difficult and the healing of apostemes is delayed by nature; or because there is a bone within it, or a number of bones.
And I have already shown all these causes and their signs, as well as their treatments with medicines, in the division; and here it is necessary for me to make you know the treatment of fistulas and ulcers that is done by the way of surgical intervention with the hand.
Know then that a fistula can occur in all parts of the body. For there are fistulas which reach large veins and arteries, or nerves, or the liver; or the intestines, or the bladder, or one of the ribs; or one of the vertebrae of the back, or one of the joints formed by the composition, such as the hand and foot; and there are those which extend to the vicinity of the main member, and similar ones.  />
This fistula, according to this method, is difficult to heal due to the disease, and does not accept treatment; dealing with it is laborious and full of ignorance.
But if the fistula is of any kind whose depth does not reach these places that I have mentioned; and you hope and trust in its cure, and wish to arrive at knowledge of it, then take a probe made of iron or copper, if the fistula extends straight, and search with it.
However, if there is a curvature in the fistula, then investigate it with a lead probe of fine quality. Because lead, due to its softness, adapts and bends around the curvature.
If the fistula has many openings, it is not possible for you to indicate its location with a probe. Therefore, irrigate one of its openings from among its openings.
For the liquid with which you irrigate it passes towards the other openings and flows out of them.
Then carefully investigate according to the way that it is possible for you: so that you may know whether there is a bone or nerve there, and whether the depth of the fistula is distant or near; or whether the fistula is one whose openings are many, and stand over all of it, with your greatest strength: with your questioning of the patient, by which you ask the sick person, and with the discovery of pain upon pressing with your hand on the place, and similar indications and accidental causes.
When you have stood over all these things with true positioning, then go to treatment with confidence. And consider then, if the fistula is appearing near or in a safe place distant from a joint, or from a nerve, or an artery, or a vein, or one of the places that I mentioned to you; then cut the fistula as was previously stated from my account, and remove what is in it by filtration, and rotten flesh that grows in its opening from flesh, or pus, and similar things: and care for it until it heals.  />
If, however, the fistula is of great depth and straight, then it is necessary that you cut as much of it out as possible. Then cleanse it from all its corrupted flesh.
Then apply a bandage soaked in sharp medicine and insert it until it reaches the hollow of the fistula that you have grasped with the iron; do this several times, until the sharp medicine has eaten away all that remains in the hollow of the fistula from the corruption.
Then treat it with ointments that promote healthy flesh until it heals.
If it does not heal through this, then cauterize it as we have described.
Therefore, if the cause of the fistula is a bone and it is certain to you, then search for it and cut it as I have told you: if nothing prevents you from the vein, nerve, or main member, as we have said.
Therefore, if a bone is revealed to you and there is some corruption or blackness in it, then scrape it until all its corruption is removed. Then treat it with what promotes healing until it heals.
If it does not heal and continues to discharge pus as before, then know that you have not reached the complete removal of the corruption.
Therefore, examine it again and make a very careful scraping and cleansing of it with all your strength.
Then treat it.  /> If it heals, that is good; if not, then know that the corruption is in a deep part of the body which you have not reached. You therefore lack skill in it, except to leave it to nature.
If the bone is small and possible for you, draw it out with fine forceps suitable for it.
If indeed there are many bones, then make a careful extraction of all of them, and do not let any slip by with your strength.
If however something from the moisture is causing trouble for you and there is no fear or error in their incisions, then cut those moistures and flesh if they are present, and free the bones.
If however you are not prepared to remove the bones at that time, then place something on the wound to cause it to putrefy; and leave it until what is around those bones from flesh and moisture putsrefies.
And guard the wound so that it does not heal over. And let the cut which you have made in your work be constricted. Or if you are afraid, place on it a cloth soaked in ground sulfur mixed with oil; or a cloth soaked in Egyptian ointment, or any green ointment.
For when those moistures have putrefied and the bones have been separated from them, their removal is made easier and their extraction also.
But if it is a large bone, such as the shinbone or the hipbone, and part of it has become corrupted; then scrape it with the finest rasp until that blackness and corruption are removed. Then restore the wound.
But if what is corrupted in it is a large part and the corruption has already reached the marrow of the bone, then it is necessary to saw it and cut it completely up to the place where the corruption reaches; then care for it until it heals over.  />   />   />
And I tell you a story which happened to a man in his leg; so that you may use it as an example and assistance for your work.
There was a young man about thirty years old, who had pain in his leg from an internal cause that moved within him; that is, from the inside, until the material reached his leg and it swelled up with a large swelling: and there was no external cause for it.
Therefore, time passed with error on the part of the physicians until the abscess burst, and many substances gathered with it. And his cure was delayed until the leg became ulcerated and many openings formed in it, which all discharged pus and bodily fluids.
Therefore, many physicians attended to him for about two years, and there was no one skilled in the art of surgery among them until I was called, and I saw his leg and the substances flowing from those openings in great quantity; indeed, all his body had already withered away, and his color was jaundiced.
Therefore, I inserted a probe into one of the openings and the probe reached the mouth.
Then I investigated all the openings and found that they were interconnected to each other from every part of the leg.
Therefore I hastened and cut over one of those openings until I exposed part of the bone, and found it corrupt, that it had already rotted away and blackened, and become putrid, and penetrated all the way to the marrow.  />
I therefore sawed off what was exposed to me, and prepared it from the rotten bone.
And I judged that there was nothing else in the bone except for that corruption which I cut away and sawed off. And I had already rooted it out.
Then I applied a wound dressing with consolidating medicines for a long time.  /> Â• And it did not heal. Â• Â•
Then I probed again and exposed the bone a second time above the first exposure, and found continuous corruption with the bone, and sawed off what appeared to me from that corruption as well.
Then I attempted to dress it. And it did not heal.
Therefore I exposed it again and did not stop cutting the bone piece by piece and trying to dress it, and it did not heal until I had cut away about a hand's breadth of bone with its marrow.
Then I restored him with medicines, and he was quickly consolidated and healed. This repetition of the operation and section would not have been necessary except for the weak condition of the patient, his limited tolerance, and my fear of his death; because he was experiencing syncope from excessive evacuation at all hours.
Thus he was completely cured; and a strong, good flesh grew in the place of the bone; his body became well-proportioned, and his strength returned; he resumed his normal habits; and there was no damage at all to his walking.
But if the projecting bone has already been broken off in the body, then you must sew it up in this way: Take a string and tie it to the end of the projecting bone; and command someone to pull it upward; and place another thicker woolen thread over the first string. Then tie it over the flesh that is next to the bone; and extend its end so as to pull the flesh downward; and you will uncover the flesh over the place where you wish to sew, so that the saw does not cut the flesh.
Place a piece of wood or board under the bone properly; for when you do this, it will not prevent the saw from cutting through the rotten flesh.
And the sawing should be slightly above the rotten spot, so that the rot is not in a hollow of the bone; and it does not appear to the touch, and thus induces an alternate method of sawing.
But if the bone is rotten and does not project outward, but rather continues connected to another part; and the rot is in its middle or side; then uncover all the flesh from all sides completely. Then place a piece of wood underneath.
Then saw through it from the first side where there is rot, until the sawing reaches the other side; and let the sawing be slightly longer than the rot, as we have said.
If corruption is in the joint, cut the corrupted joint and saw the bone where it continues on the other side.
However, if corruption is between two joints, then there is no skill in that except to scrape it off.
But if corruption is in the comb of the hand or the comb of the foot, then the matter is very difficult. Indeed, you must examine how the corruption appears to you. And scrape it off, and clean it as best you can with whatever skill is available to you: when the vein or nerve does not work against you.
And know that there are many different cutting tools and saws for cutting these bones, depending on the position of the bones, their preparation, their thickness or thinness, size, smallness, hardness, and softness. Therefore, it is necessary to prepare a suitable tool for each type of operation.
And know that these operations indicate to you the kind of tool you need when your study is prolonged.  /> And the knowledge of the methods of this art is a witness to the methods of diseases, then indeed you will find through yourself what suits it from the instruments for every ailment.
And I assure you at the end of this chapter the number of instruments that you will use as examples for what you cut, and a test by which you try others.
The shape of another saw.
The form of the knife for joints. Let the head of this knife be in the shape of a star-headed nail: and its points should be in the shape of the points of the elischetfegi.
And it is not suitable except to smooth the heads of joints when they are injured, whether a large or great bone is present.

The form of the broad knife.
The form of the knife which has a concavity.
The form of another fine knife.
The form of another knife with a curved tip.
The form of the small and delicate needle-like knife.
This resembles a file, and its tip is like a saw; it is used in many places for the sake of cutting bones. xspace
The form of the knife suitable for removing that which has been perforated from the bone.
Its tip is triangular and its points are sharp.
It is made of iron. And similarly, all that we have mentioned should be made from knives and saws.
Â¶ On the cutting of tips and sawing of bones.
The tips become putrid either from an external cause or from an internal one.  /> Caput XC.
Therefore, when you have treated that putrefaction with medicines and the treatment does not help, and you see the putrefaction spread into a limb which is not affected by anything else: then it is necessary for you to cut off that limb up to where the putrefaction has reached, so that the patient may escape from death or from the greater evil of loss of the limb.
And the sign of that which occurs is that the member darkens until it appears to be burnt by fire or decayed after blackening; until that decay spreads to the point where it follows that member and creeps throughout the whole body.
Therefore, hasten with its incision, and similarly if the cause of decay is from the bite of certain venomous creatures, such as the marine scorpion, viper, or asp, and similar ones.
If therefore the decay or bite is on the tip of a finger, then cut off the finger, and do not leave space for the decay to advance to the rest of the hand.
And similarly, if it occurs on the hand, then cut it off at the root of the wrist, and do not leave space for the decay to reach the forearm.
And if it invades that [forearm], then cut off the arm at the elbow joint.
If, however, the decay passes through and you see it around the elbow, then death is certain for the patient. And beyond that, administering from the treatment is a matter of skill.
And similarly, do the same with the foot when decay invades a toe; then cut it off at one of the joints. If it reaches the sole of the foot, then cut off the entire foot. If it however advances to the knee, then cut off the leg at the knee joint.
When decay has already reached above the knee, then there is no skill [to save him], except to abandon and leave the patient to death.
And the method of cutting or sawing a member is to tie a ligature below the place you wish to cut and tie another ligature above that place. And let one assistant pull the lower ligature downward, and let another assistant pull the upper ligature upward. And you separate the flesh that is between the two ligatures with a broad scalpel until all the flesh is laid bare. Then it should be cut or sewn.
And you should place a cloth of linen over all parts, so that the saw does not touch the healthy area; and it may happen that an additional injury is inflicted on the sick person, and a hot abscess forms.
But if bleeding occurs internally while you are operating, then quickly cauterize the area, or place some powders that absorb blood on it. Then return to your treatment until it is completed.
Then bind the wounded limb with a suitable bandage and care for it until it heals.
And I tell you that this happened to a man on his foot, the same event as I am telling you.
Which is to say that a blackening occurred on his foot, similar to the burning of fire; and this corruption first began in his toe until it spread to his entire foot.
Therefore the man hastened to cut himself off, after he saw that the corruption was advancing into his limb with great intensity, which he found from the pain and burning of it; and he cut himself at the joint, and he was healed.
And after a long time had passed, that same corruption occurred in his index finger of his hand.
So he came to me, and I tried to draw out that excess with the ointment I placed on his hand after cleansing his body; but the swelling did not subside, and began spreading to another finger until the corruption spread to the whole hand.
So he called upon me to cut off his hand; and I refused, hoping for the subsiding of that swelling from me; and I also feared death at cutting off his hand. âž¤ Because the man's strength was greater than the condition.
So after he despaired of me, he returned to his own land; and news came to me about him that he had hastened and cut off his whole hand; and he was healed.
And I did not bring forward this narrative except to be of assistance concerning that which falls under the category of this illness: and so that it may serve as a signifier by which is indicated, and according to which one should act.
About caring for the sinuses, and the quality of enema administration with medications.
When an abscess occurs in some fleshy members and the space of the abscess is prolonged until it forms a collection of pus: then it bursts or perforates, and what is within it comes out as pus, and the place remains empty like a vessel: and the skin that is above it is like a cloth that has already been made thin: and it does not reach to the end in its corruption, neither imprinting on a bone, nor on a nerve, nor on a ligament: it deserves to be called a Sinus; and it is not called a Fistula. However, if its space is prolonged until the corruption imprints on any of these members, then it is called a Fistula or fistula.
And its treatment is that you should cut off all that skin as if you were rolling it up: and especially when it has been made thin, like a cloth: and you trust that it does not adhere to the place because of its corruption.
But if you hope that the skin adheres, and it does not follow from this final corruption; and if there is thickness in the skin of flesh, then treat it with an enema: and it is as if for a sinus.
Then if it is large, and the pus that comes out of it has a foul odor: then enema it with Egyptian medication, which is vinegar, oil, and sumac, receiving equal parts, gathered together in a vessel; and boil them over fire until the medication becomes red: and reaches the consistency of honey.
Then take what you need from it, dissolve it with water and honey, and use this mixture as an enema for the bladder; then tie off its opening and leave the medicine inside for two hours.
Then draw it out with a suppository. Do this for as many days as are necessary until the bladder is cleansed and the stench removed.
And sometimes it should be irrigated with ashes water when this medicine is not available to you. Take the ashes of vine wood or holm oak wood and pour them over the water. Then strain it and use it for an enema until you are confident that the bladder is now clean.
But if the patient cannot bear the Egyptian medicine or ashes water, then use an enema of water and honey into which some powdered ginger has already been mixed. Or irrigate it with a mixture of honey and wine, because it is the nature of honey to cleanse and wash, and wine causes the bladder to adhere, especially when the wine is somewhat astringent and dry.
When you have done this several times and are confident that the corruption of the bladder has been removed, then irrigate it with what causes flesh to grow there.
And this is done by taking some diachylon plaster and dissolving it with rose oil and astringent wine; or you can irrigate it with certain other medicines and ointments whose properties I have written about in the treatise on ointments.
But if the opening of the bladder is too narrow to accept an enema cannula, then dilate it briefly with an iron instrument; or insert into it a tampon wrapped in Egyptian ointment or basilicum ointment until it is sufficiently dilated.
And similarly, if the opening is also large, then gather its lips with a stitch; and leave from it the amount into which a clyster may enter without addition.
And similarly, if the opening from which the pus flows is elevated upwards; then cut into it in the deeper part that is within it, so that the pus may flow downwards: for when pus is constricted in the depth of the Sinus, it prevents flesh from growing there.
If it is not possible for you to cut the Sinus lower as you wish; then strive to prepare the membrane with a preparation that allows the pus to flow easily according to how it is prepared for you. Strive that nothing at all of the pus be retained within it; and take healing ointments which are applied to the wound, suitable for what you wish. And spread them on a linen cloth. And let the cloth be of such size that it may cover the entire Sinus. Then cut with scissors a hole directly in the orifice of the Sinus, a little wider than the orifice of the Sinus. Then spread gentle ointments on another cloth according to the size of the hole; and place it over the Sinus, distant from its orifice, so that the exit of the pus from it may be relieved; and do not remove the large cloth, except after a few days once.
But the one that is over the orifice of the Sinus; it is this one which you remove in every hour, so that what accumulates within it from pus may exit; and so that you may know whether that which flows out of it is much or little; or digested or undigested.
And with this again consider the place of the Sinus itself; whether the master of it feels pain within it, or if there is no pain in it, and whether there is a swelling within it, or if there is no swelling in it.
When your treatment is extended in this manner and you see the material exiting from the opening of the sinus, then know that the sinus has adhered or is approaching adhesion; therefore, dissolve it in the morning or on the third day. And when you dissolve the wound, then change the cloth for another one and renew the ointment.
But if a thin pus exits from the sinus after a long period, then do not despair of its adhesion, for its healing is approaching, since there are people who slow down the growth of flesh in their wounds, and there are those who act contrary to that.
But if after many days an undigested pus exits from the sinus, then know that the sinus has not adhered.
If therefore the adhesion of the sinus is delayed and its course prolonged, then add to the drying of medicines; but let the physicians make sure that the medicines are humid in their substance and dry in their power, like the ointment called dyafinicon when a superfluous amount of egg is added.
And from the above-mentioned treatment, it is that you should take the ointment called dyafinicon and dissolve it with rose oil, and pour over it an equal amount of old wine in its substance.
Then prepare it with this, and use it.
And now perform a similar action when you do not have the ointment called dyafinicon present; for honey, when you boil it until it thickens, and use it. Or take myrrh, aloe, and frankincense; grind all of them together and powder it over the honey while it is on the fire. Then line it with a cloth and tie it over the sinus; and line it with the honey you have boiled until it thickens, and powder over it spices, and place a cloth over it, and tie it.  ///
And sometimes it is given with long birthwort, and root of the heavenly lily, and lily: and flour of the herb, and centaurie. Use them either as simples or mixed together; pound them and sift them; then powderize over the honey I mentioned, and use it.
But if the abscess is prolonged and does not heal with this treatment, then know that there is a corruption in its depth; either it is already making an impression on the bones, or on the other hard members, or on the ligaments; then treat it with the treatment of fistulas, as has been mentioned before.  /> 133
On the care of a whitlow and crushed nail, and the cutting of the finger, and its sectioning.
A whitlow is an abscess that arises under the thumbnail of the hand or foot; and perhaps it can arise in the other fingers as well.
But when the abscess is prolonged and its treatment is neglected and it becomes a hot abscess; or it is corrupted and emits pus until it gnaws at the root of the nail; and perhaps it corrupts it entirely, and perhaps the corruption reaches the bone, so that there is a foul odor; and the tip of the finger becomes swollen, and its color becomes dark.
Therefore, when you treat it with what we said in the section on division, and your treatment is not effective; then you must cut off with a knife all the remaining excess from the nail. Then cauterize the wound after that. For cautery is very beneficial.  /> 135 Â•
But if the bone is healthy and the nail is also healthy, and the additions of the nail now press the flesh inward and begin to prick it and hurt it; then you must place a fine wire under the corner of the nail that pricks the flesh, and push it upwards; and cut off that part of the flesh with ease, and put on what remains of the medicinal substances that burn and corrode until all of it is removed. Then care for it with ointments until it heals.
But if the corruption has already begun in the ulcer, then it is necessary that you cut into that ulcer and remove it; for it will never heal as long as there remains a corrupted ulcer within it.
If you see the gangrene and corruption advancing into the finger, then cut it at one of its joints, as was mentioned earlier in its description. Then care for it until it heals.
But if it happens that the nail is worn down or struck: and there arises a severe pain from it, then it is necessary to bleed the patient first. Then cut the nail with an acutely pointed spatula, making a transverse section from top to bottom as you see fit.
And take care that the section does not reach the flesh beneath the nail, for you will cause a very severe pain to occur through this over the patient, and there will be an additional cause of scarring in that place.
Then care for the place with something that soothes the pains.
But the extra finger that is born in some people's hands is perhaps entirely fleshy; and perhaps there are bones in some of them, and perhaps there is a nail on it; and sometimes it is born at the root of the joint, or its birth is in some of the finger's joints. Therefore, that which is born in some of the finger's joints does not move; and that which is born at the finger's joint, perhaps moves.
The section of those which are fleshy is easy. Which is to say: cut it at its root with a broad spatula.  /> Et sic de iuncturae addita: et similiter quae sunt in manibus aliorum, et est eisdem remediis curanda, et idem est modus curandi eorum.
However, the cure for that whose birth is at the root of the joint is difficult. Avoid cutting it.
But if it is born on a finger at the last joint, then you should cut its flesh with a round incision right up to the bone. Then saw the bone with one of those suitable saws for it. Then care for it until it heals.
A contraction that occurs between fingers can often happen due to a birth defect, that is, it is born with it, or from the healing of a wound, or a burn from fire, and similar causes.  />
Therefore, you must cut away that contraction until the fingers return to their natural shape. Then place between them bandages or cloths soaked in rose oil, so that they do not quickly heal together, and separate them; or place between them a thin sheet of lead until the place heals as it should.
And similarly, if a contraction occurs between some fingers and the palm, then cut away that contraction according to what is prepared and suitable for the shape of the limb.
Â¶ On the incision of a tumor.
Veins are swollen, thick, full of melancholic excesses that occur in many parts of the body; and most of their occurrences are in the legs, especially in the legs of travelers and workers and bearers.
Therefore, you must administer a purgative made from black bile several times with a strong laxative.
Then bleed the patient from those veins.
Their treatment with iron is in two ways.  /> â— If it is on a small part of the body or not very swollen: then incise it gently, and extract what is inside it, and cauterize it so that it does not swell again.  /> â— But if it is large or very swollen: then cut away its skin, and take out what is in it, and stitch up the wound with silk thread until the swelling goes down. ã€‹ One of these methods is to cut them open and extract the black blood. And another method is to lift the vein and remove it entirely.
Its section is according to this manner. First, soak the leg with very hot water until the thick and feculent blood dissolves. Then tie off the patient's leg from the top of the thigh to below the knee with a bandage. Then cut the vein in one place, or two, or three, with a wide incision.
Then lift, that is, draw out the blood into your hand from the lower part of the leg up to the top, and first of all, let the phlebotomist bleed the patient. Then cut the nail along with it below: until enough blood comes out as you see fit and which the patient's strength can bear.
Afterwards, tie it off and instruct the patient to abstain from foods that generate black bile. Repeat the evacuation and bloodletting whenever the veins are full and it harms the patient.
Its lifting is according to this manner. Shave the leg of the patient if it has many hairs. Then put the patient into a bath or soak his leg in hot water until it becomes red and the veins swell, or if there is no bath available, exercise strongly until the limb warms up.
Then cut the skin along the length of the vein's path: either at its end near the knee or at its lower part near the heel.
Then open the skin with hooks and strip the vein from all sides until it is visible to the touch, and at its appearance you will see it redden towards blackness. When it emerges from the skin, you will see it white like a string.
Then insert under it a reed until when lifted and emerges from the skin; hang it with a blind hook, soft.
Then cut another incision near that incision three fingers wide. Then scrape away the skin from above the vein until it appears. Then lift it with tongs as you did before, and hang it with another hook as you did at first.
Then cut another incision or several more if you need to. Then lift it and cut it off at the last incision near the heel.
Then draw it out to the incision above it.
And do this until you draw it out from the uppermost or all of the incisions, when it comes out entirely; then cut it off.
But if it does not obey you by being drawn out and lifted up, then insert a needle with a strong double thread and tie it off, and draw it out; or insert under it a hook: and turn your hand to every side until it comes out. And be careful that it is not cut.  /> For if it is cut, it will be very difficult for you to lift it up, and harm may come to the patient from that.
When you have drawn it out entirely, then place over the wound a woolen cloth soaked in wine and rose oil or oil, and care for him until he is healed.
But if the vein is constricted and has a tortuous course which it follows to its parts, and is not straight as we have said, then you must slit over it along every part of its tortuous course and places of its twisting.
Then hang it with hooks until you lift it all out; and be careful at your incision above it that you do not cut the vein or injure it, for it will become very difficult for you to lift or draw it out. Therefore keep your discretion.

The shape of a blind tumor.
It does not have the convexity of other tumors, nor the sharp extremities so as not to wound a vein; and it is large and twisted, soft: because if it were thin, it would pierce the vein with its thinness; but it must have excessive thickness, as we said.
On the Extraction of the Vein of the Leg.
This vein is generated in the legs in hot lands, such as Alizegi and the Arabian land, and in dry, hot lands where there is little tenderness, that is, where neither grass nor trees grow.
And perhaps it is generated in other parts of the body besides the legs. xspace
And its generation is due to putrefaction occurring under the skin, just as happens within bodies with serpents and worms called ascarids, and the worms generated between the skin and flesh.
And the sign of the beginning of this vein's appearance is that a severe inflammation occurs in the leg. Then the spot becomes blistered. Then the vein begins to emerge from that blistered spot, as if it were a root of a plant or an animal.
Therefore, when its extremity becomes visible from that, then you should wrap around it a piece of lead weighing one drachm and two nqbats, and leave the suspended lead hanging from the leg.
So whenever something emerges out of it to the outside, wrap that in lead and tie it up. If it becomes very long, then cut off a piece of it and wrap the rest. And do not cut it off at its root before all of it has emerged.  ?> If you cut, it contracts and enters into the flesh, causing an abscess and putrefaction in the place, and a bad sore.
Therefore, it should be treated gently and extracted gradually until it comes out from its last part, so that nothing remains of it in the body; and this vein, in certain people, extends to a length of five palms and ten. And now it has come to me because it came out of a man from twenty palms.
But if it is cut during your treatment time, then insert a reed into its opening and perforate it with a long hole along with the body until everything that is in it from matter is evacuated; and administer treatments for putrefaction of the place for several days. Then treat him according to the method for treating abscesses.
And this vein sometimes has many branches, especially when it appears at the ankle or in the foot itself; and there are many openings for it, and from each opening a branch comes out.
Therefore treat it as we have said in the division, along with what was stated beforehand.
Â¶ On cutting above worms generated under the skin, which is called bovine disease.
This disease is called in a certain land among us bovine disease because it often happens to cows and it is a small worm that is born between the skin and flesh.
And it goes through the entire body, ascending and descending; and it is felt when walking from member to member until it breaks through wherever it breaks through the skin and comes out.
And its generation is from the putrefaction of certain humors. Just as worms and snakes, that is, earthworms and roundworms, occur in the belly.  />
And fear is caused by its malignancy. Because when it goes into the body and is raised to the head and reaches that place, then perhaps it opens up there and exits, and destroys the eye, and this often happens.
Therefore, when you want to cure it and extract it, this is only done during its movement and appearance to the senses.
You must therefore tie strongly with a ligature what is above it and what is below it. Then cut above it and extract it.
But if it goes deep into the flesh and you cannot find it, then put a cautery with fire on that place until it dies.
And what is even more feared is its corruption, by which it corrupts the eye, as we have said.
But if you see that it has already reached near the eye at the head, then tie a good ligature under it on the eyebrow. Then cut above it and extract it. abei
And the patient must use bodily cleansing with medicines that dissolve bad putrid humors.
And he should avoid foods that cause putrefaction.
Â¶ On the incision for Nakir's disease.
This disease is called Nakir in our land, and it is a pain that occurs in certain limbs, then changes from one limb to another.
And I myself have already seen this, as I am telling you. I was called to a sick woman in certain villages. beyi beyi And she uncovered her arm, and I saw a small swelling on the tendon of the arm vein.
And after I remained for one hour, I saw a swelling go forth like a caterpillar, moving quickly up her arm to the shoulder faster than is possible, just as silver moves when it runs from place to place.
The pain then retreated from that place and fixed itself in the shoulder.
Then I sat for an hour, and it ran through the rest of the body until it reached the other arm.
Then he told me that it was turning throughout his whole body, as I saw.
So I marveled at the speed with which it changed from member to member. And truly, before that, I had never seen this illness in my eyes acting in such a way. However, I have seen many people in whom pain was transferred from member to member; but I had never seen it with my own eyes as I saw it in the woman.
And I do not think that this happened except because she was one of those women with dry bodies and visible veins; from which it seems to the senses that the wind was transferred.
And it is necessary that these do not appear according to this reasoning in those who are delicate and have moist bodies with hidden veins.  />
Therefore, when you want to treat it and the patient feels that pain, then if it is visible to your eye as we have said, quickly tie above it and below it; and cut above it until that wind comes out constricted; and cauterize the place.
But if you do not see it with your own eyes, then treat it with bodily evacuation and with what expels winds and binds them with fetid pills, and pills of serpentaria, and similar things.
Â§ On the Extraction of Arrows.  />
Arrows are distinguished by their kinds and by the places where they fall from the body.
Their diversity is such that some have large heads and others small; some are hollow and others solid. And among them are those which have three angles. And among these are tongues. And among these are stars.
However, those which fall according to the members are of two kinds. For the members are either from the principal hollow organs, such as the brain, heart, liver, lung, kidney, intestine, bladder, and similar things. Therefore, when it falls into one of these members and the signs of death, which I will tell you later, appear to you, then you must avoid extracting that arrow from them, because death follows him in whom it is, in many cases. And when these bad signs do not appear to you and the arrow is not hidden deep within the member, then extract it and treat the wound.
For the signs of the brain when an arrow falls into it and penetrates the bone and exits through the fontanel on top of the brain are: because there occurs from it a severe headache, blindness in one eye, dizziness, redness of the eyes, swelling, redness of the tongue, spasms, confusion, and vomiting of bile. And perhaps blood will come out of the nose or ears. And perhaps speech is cut off and the voice destroyed. And a white fluid like dough comes out of the place of the wound. And from it comes something resembling the wateriness of meat.  />
If therefore these signs appear to you, then refrain from treating it, and extract the arrow if it has not exited.
The signs of the arrow when it falls into the heart are that it is near the left nipple and feels as if it is stuck in a hard thing, not an empty one. And perhaps there is a movement in the arrow similar to the pulse and black blood runs from the wound.  /> 89463217 And it is followed by coldness in the extremities, cold sweat, and fainting. You should know that death has certainly come.
And the sign of an arrow wound to the lung is that blood-froth comes out of the wound; and the veins that follow the neck become inflamed, and the color of the sick person changes. And he exhales a great deal of air with great force; and seeks to inhale cold air.
If the arrow falls on the diaphragm which is in the chest, then it is close to the small ribs; and there is a great gasping with severe pain and sighing; and all the limbs of the shoulders tremble.
And if the arrow falls on the stomach, then perhaps something undigested comes out of the wound from food.
And if the arrow falls on the belly and pierces it, then something of fecal matter comes out of the wound, or an intestine that has already been torn. There is therefore no hope for his cure, nor in extracting the arrow.
If the arrow falls on the bladder and urine comes out; and something comes out of it to the outside, and the pain is greater on the sick person; then you should know that it is fatal.
The remaining limbs, such as the face, and neck, and throat, and shoulder blade, and shoulder joint, and back of the loins, and collarbone, and hip, and leg, and others like them from the limbs are healed according to various dispositions; when the arrow does not find a main artery or nerve; and is not a poisoned arrow. ã€‹ ã€‹
And I tell you that I have seen of these arrows, in order for you to know through this concerning your cure.
That is, because a certain man had an arrow fall on his tear duct at the root of his nose. I removed it from her other side, under the fat of her ear; and she was healed, and no harm came to her eye.
I also removed an arrow from a Jew that had fallen into his eyelid fat under the lower eyelid; and the arrow was already hidden, and I could not get anything but its small end, which was attached to its shaft: and it was a large arrow of the Turkish bows, with a soft iron tip, in which there are no barbs.
Therefore, the Jew was healed, and no evil befell his eye.
And I removed another arrow from a Christian's throat.
And it was an Arab arrow, and that is the type with barbs. I cut, therefore, above it between the two rings: and it was already sunk into his throat. Therefore, I became skilled with it, until I removed it; and the Christian was healed. />
And I removed another arrow from a man that had fallen into his belly; and we thought that he would die from it.
Therefore, after thirty days had passed and nothing changed in his condition, I cut above the arrow; and I sharpened it, and removed it; and he was healed, and no evil befell him.
And I saw a man on whom an arrow had fallen into his back, and the wound over it had become healed. Therefore, after seven years had passed, the arrow came out at the base of his thigh.
And I saw a woman on whom an arrow had fallen into her belly, and the wound over it had become healed, and the arrow remained inside her; and nothing changed in her condition, and the woman did not find any harm in any of her natural functions.
And I saw another man who was struck by an arrow in his face; the wound hardened and remained, causing him little pain. There were many similar cases like this.
And I removed an arrow from a man who was one of the king's nobles; it had struck him in the middle of his nose and slightly deviated to the right side, and the entire arrow was hidden.
I was therefore called to treat him three days after the incident with the arrow. I found that the arrow wound was very tight.
So I examined it with a fine probe and did not feel it; the man himself found pain and discomfort under his right ear. Therefore, I hoped that this was a point of exit from the tip of the arrow.
I then applied a plaster with attracting and digesting powers to the area, hoping that the wound would suppurate and reveal to me the sign of the arrow so that I could cut over it; but this did not happen, indicating that the arrow had not reached that location.
I continued to apply the plaster for many days, and no discharge occurred; the wound healed, but the man remained weak from the arrow's removal for some time until one day he felt the arrow inside his nose. And he told me about it.
And he told me about it. So I placed a sharp, corrosive medicine on the wound for many days until it opened up; and when I probed it with a probe, I felt the tip of the arrow attached to the wood.
Then I continued to widen the wound with that sharp medicine until we could see the tip of the arrow visibly; and this process took about four months.
Then after the wound had been widened enough to allow me to insert forceps into it and move the arrow, but it did not exit; I did not stop refining and inventing methods for removing it until one day I began with well-made forceps, as will be shown in their form at the end of this chapter, until I removed it. Then I repaired the wound.
And indeed, doctors judge that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored. Therefore I repaired it (the cartilage of the nose), and the wound was healed, and the patient was restored to full health; nothing whatever harmed him.
And I tell you about the method of extracting certain arrows: so that you may use this as a rule and understanding for what I did not say.
Since the parts of this art and their distinctions are not comprehended by mere narrative; nor does the book comprehend them, but a skillful craftsman compares a little to much, and what is present to what is absent; and he finds a new operation and a new instrument in dealing with external things of this art when they occur.  />
I say therefore that arrows do not exit from the members to which they are fixed except in two ways. Either by retracing their path back out of the place where they entered. Or through the opposite side (of the body).
And those that exit where they entered are either arrows passing through fleshy parts, which can be drawn out and exit.  />
But if it does not yield to exit at the time it fell, then you must leave it for some days until the flesh around it putrefies, and its extraction will be facilitated, along with its exit.
Similarly, if it is embedded in bone and does not yield to you for extraction, then leave it also for some days; and every day try to extract it with traction and motion, until it comes out.
But if after several days it does not yield to you for extraction, then you must bore around the arrow in the bone itself from all sides with a fine awl, until the arrow becomes enlarged. Then draw it out and extract it.
But if the arrow is already hidden in some part of the body and is concealed and hidden from sense, then seek it out with a probe. But if you feel it, then extract it with certain instruments that are suitable for its extraction.
But if you cannot reach it because of the narrowness of the wound and the length of the arrow deep inside, and there is no bone, nerve, or vein there, then cut open above it until the wound is widened and it becomes possible to extract the arrow.
But if there are ears (i.e., pieces of flesh) by which it is held, then free the attached flesh from every side and in every way you can manage to do that, and if it cannot be extracted because of the breaking of the ears and their twisting, then persist until it comes out. )))
And when you administer the extraction of an arrow in whatever place it is, then use the twisting of your hand with forceps on all parts until you make it come out; and be subtle with the utmost subtlety so that the arrow does not break and its attraction and extraction become difficult for you.
If you cannot cut it in one hour, then leave it for some days until what surrounds it decays. Then repeat the process; the swelling will be relieved. However, if the flow of blood is causing difficulty for you, then administer what we said in its own chapter on treatment: and guard your virtue from cutting a vein or nerve or sinew.
And administer the medicine in every way that is possible for you to evade the arrow: and let it be with ease, calmness, slowness, and firmness, as I have told you.
And it is necessary that when you draw the arrow, it should be weakened according to the figure as it was at the time of the arrow wound itself. Because it is more beneficial. If this is not possible for you, then administer what is possible from the figures.
If the arrow comes out of the opposite part, or something is already protruding to the outside, or if it forms a swelling at the tip of the arrow that you can feel under the skin and see it protruding, cut above it; let the incision be according to the size that the forceps can grasp in it.  ()
Then draw it out, for it becomes easy to remove.
But if it is lodged in the bone, then twist your hand according to its roundness until the arrow presses into the bone and enlarges its own opening; then draw it out.
And if not, leave it for some days; then repeat the process until it comes out.
If the arrow has a wooden shaft, then push it out with its shaft.  ()
But if the wooden shaft has broken off and you wish to administer a push, then insert into it a concave instrument so that its concavity enters into the tail of the arrow; then push it out with it.  ()  ()  ()  ()
If however the arrow is barbed, then push it through with an entering instrument. For the arrow should be removed by that means.
If the arrow is poisoned, then it is necessary to cut out all the flesh in which the poison is located, if it is possible for you. Then treat it with what is suitable for that.
If the arrow falls into the chest or belly or bladder or side and is close to the surface so that you can feel it with your finger, and it is possible for you to cut above it, then cut, and be careful not to cut a vein or nerve, and extract it.
Then treat the wound, if you see it, until it heals.
And this is the form of the forceps with which arrows are extracted.
The ends should be like the beak of a bird and made in such a way that when they grasp the arrow, they do not let it go.
And many forms are made from them, large and small and medium, according to the size of the arrow and its narrowness, and the width of the wound and its narrowness.
